</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L119" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="119"></td>
        <td id="LC119" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\title</span>{Multiplicative Hitchin Systems and Supersymmetric Gauge Theory}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L120" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="120"></td>
        <td id="LC120" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\author</span>{Chris Elliott <span class="pl-c1">\and</span> Vasily Pestun}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L121" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="121"></td>
        <td id="LC121" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\date</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\today</span>}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L122" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="122"></td>
        <td id="LC122" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L123" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="123"></td>
        <td id="LC123" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{document}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L124" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="124"></td>
        <td id="LC124" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L125" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="125"></td>
        <td id="LC125" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\maketitle</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L126" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="126"></td>
        <td id="LC126" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{abstract}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L127" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="127"></td>
        <td id="LC127" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Multiplicative Hitchin systems are analogues of Hitchin&#39;s integrable system based on moduli spaces of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs bundles on a curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where the Higgs field is group-valued, rather than Lie algebra valued.  We discuss the relationship between several occurences of these moduli spaces in geometry and supersymmetric gauge theory, with a particular focus on the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a fixed framing at infinity.  In this case we prove that the identification between multiplicative Higgs bundles and periodic monopoles proved by Charbonneau and Hurtubise can be promoted to an equivalence of hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler spaces, and analyze the twistor rotation for the multiplicative Hitchin system.  We also discuss quantization of these moduli spaces, yielding the modules for the Yangian <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> discovered by Gerasimov, Kharchev, Lebedev and Oblezin.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L128" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="128"></td>
        <td id="LC128" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{abstract}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L129" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="129"></td>
        <td id="LC129" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L130" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="130"></td>
        <td id="LC130" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\vspace</span>{5pt}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L131" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="131"></td>
        <td id="LC131" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">{<span class="pl-c1">\bf</span> Keywords:} Hitchin system, monopoles, hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structures, supersymmetric gauge theory, topological twists, Yangian quantum group (AMS Subject Classification: 53D30, 14D21, 81T60).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L132" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="132"></td>
        <td id="LC132" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L133" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="133"></td>
        <td id="LC133" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Introduction}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L134" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="134"></td>
        <td id="LC134" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L135" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="135"></td>
        <td id="LC135" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this paper, we will compare five different perspectives on a single moduli space: three coming from geometry and representation theory, and two coming from supersymmetric gauge theory.  By leveraging these multiple perspectives we&#39;ll equip our common moduli space with the structure of a completely integrable system which we call the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{multiplicative Hitchin system}.  Many of the structures associated with the ordinary Hitchin system, such as the brane of opers, have parallels in the multiplicative setting.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L136" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="136"></td>
        <td id="LC136" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L137" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="137"></td>
        <td id="LC137" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us begin by presenting these five perspectives, before explaining their inter-relationships.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a Riemann surface, and let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a reductive complex Lie group.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L138" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="138"></td>
        <td id="LC138" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L139" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="139"></td>
        <td id="LC139" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L140" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="140"></td>
        <td id="LC140" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Multiplicative Higgs Bundles}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L141" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="141"></td>
        <td id="LC141" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll first describe the moduli space that motivates the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L142" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="142"></td>
        <td id="LC142" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">``multiplicative Hitchin system&#39;&#39; terminology.  Say that a</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L143" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="143"></td>
        <td id="LC143" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{multiplicative Higgs bundle} on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L144" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="144"></td>
        <td id="LC144" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a meromorphic automorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> P <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L145" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="145"></td>
        <td id="LC145" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">equivalently, a meromorphic section of the group-valued adjoint bundle</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L146" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="146"></td>
        <td id="LC146" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We refer to these by analogy with Higgs bundles, which</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L147" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="147"></td>
        <td id="LC147" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">consist of a meromorphic section of the Lie algebra (co)adjoint</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L148" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="148"></td>
        <td id="LC148" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">bundle, rather than its Lie group valued analogue <span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{Usually</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L149" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="149"></td>
        <td id="LC149" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Higgs bundles on a curve are defined to be sections of the coadjoint</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L150" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="150"></td>
        <td id="LC150" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  bundle twisted by the canonical bundle.  There isn&#39;t an obvious</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L151" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="151"></td>
        <td id="LC151" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  replacement for this twist in the multiplicative context, but we&#39;ll</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L152" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="152"></td>
        <td id="LC152" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  mostly be interested in the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is Calabi-Yau, and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L153" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="153"></td>
        <td id="LC153" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  therefore this twist is trivial.}.  Just like for ordinary Higgs</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L154" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="154"></td>
        <td id="LC154" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">bundles, the space of multiplicative meromorphic Higgs bundles with</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L155" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="155"></td>
        <td id="LC155" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">arbitrary poles is infinite-dimensional, but we can cut it down to a</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L156" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="156"></td>
        <td id="LC156" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">finite-dimensional space by fixing the locations of the singularities,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L157" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="157"></td>
        <td id="LC157" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and their local behaviour at each singular point.  For example, for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> this local behaviour is given by a degree at each puncture: we restrict to multiplicative Higgs fields <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> such that, near each singular point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given by the product of a local holomorphic function and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z-z_i)^{n_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for some integer <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More generally the local ``degrees&#39;&#39; are described by orbits in the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L158" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="158"></td>
        <td id="LC158" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">affine Grassmannian <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: restrict the multiplicative Higgs field</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L159" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="159"></td>
        <td id="LC159" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">to a formal neighborhood of the puncture, to obtain an element of the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L160" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="160"></td>
        <td id="LC160" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">algebraic loop group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>LG = G(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This element is well-defined</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L161" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="161"></td>
        <td id="LC161" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">up to the action of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^+G = G[[z]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on the left and right, and so</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L162" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="162"></td>
        <td id="LC162" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">determines a well-defined double coset in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L163" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="163"></td>
        <td id="LC163" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^+G <span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span> LG/L^+G = L^+G <span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Orbits in the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L164" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="164"></td>
        <td id="LC164" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">affine Grassmannian are in canonical bijection with dominant coweights</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L165" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="165"></td>
        <td id="LC165" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so fixing a ``degree&#39;&#39; at the punctures means fixing a dominant</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L166" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="166"></td>
        <td id="LC166" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">coweight <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at each puncture <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L167" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="167"></td>
        <td id="LC167" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L168" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="168"></td>
        <td id="LC168" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> Fix a curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and consider the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles} on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with prescribed singularities lying at the points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, z_k<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, with degrees <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{z_1}^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{z_k}^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> respectively.  We denote this moduli space by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L169" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="169"></td>
        <td id="LC169" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L170" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="170"></td>
        <td id="LC170" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> Moduli spaces of multiplicative Higgs bundles have been studied in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L171" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="171"></td>
        <td id="LC171" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> the literature previously, though they&#39;ve more often been referred to</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L172" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="172"></td>
        <td id="LC172" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> simply as ``moduli spaces of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-pairs&#39;&#39;.  The earliest mathematical  descriptions of these moduli spaces that we&#39;re aware of is in the work of Arutyunov, Frolov, and Medvedev <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Arutyunov:1996vy,Arutyunov:1996uw} in the integrable systems literature, for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>(n)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-pairs of zero degree on an elliptic curve, extended by Braden, Chernyakov, Dolgushev, Levin, Olshanetsky</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L173" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="173"></td>
        <td id="LC173" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> and Zotov <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Chernyakov:2007,Braden:2003gf} to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>(n)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-pairs of non-zero degree.  For a general reductive group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, moduli spaces of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-pairs were studied in the work of Hurtubise and Markman <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{HurtubiseMarkman, HurtubiseMarkman1}, from a more geometric perspective.  Their work was motivated by the desire to understand the elliptic Skylanin Poisson brackets on</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L174" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="174"></td>
        <td id="LC174" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> loop groups, and to that end they too mainly studied the case where the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L175" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="175"></td>
        <td id="LC175" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> underlying curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is elliptic -- we&#39;ll refer back to their work</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L176" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="176"></td>
        <td id="LC176" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> throughout the paper.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L177" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="177"></td>
        <td id="LC177" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L178" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="178"></td>
        <td id="LC178" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> From a different perspective, the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles was also studied by Frenkel and Ng<span class="pl-cce">\^</span>o <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 4]{FrenkelNgo} as part of their geometrization of the trace formula.  Further work was done following their definition by Bouthier <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Bouthier2, Bouthier1}, who gave an alternative construction of the moduli space as the space of sections of a vector bundle associated to a fixed singuarity datum defined using the Vinberg semigroup (see Remark <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Bouthier_remark}).  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L179" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="179"></td>
        <td id="LC179" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L180" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="180"></td>
        <td id="LC180" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> The moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles admits a version of the Hitchin fibration, just like the ordinary moduli space of Higgs bundles.  Intuitively, this map is defined using the Chevalley map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> G <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (for instance if <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the map sending a matrix to its characteristic polynomial): the multiplicative Higgs field is, in particular, a meromorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued function, and the multiplicative Hitchin fibration post-composes this function with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  See Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Hitchin_system_section} for a more detailed definition.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L181" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="181"></td>
        <td id="LC181" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L182" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="182"></td>
        <td id="LC182" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> While the structure of the multiplicative fibration makes sense for any curve, it only defines a completely integrable system -- in particular there is only a natural symplectic structure on the total space -- in the very special situation where the curve $C$ is Calabi-Yau.  That is, $C$ must be either $\CC$, $\CC^\times$ or an elliptic curve.  In this paper we&#39;ll be most interested in the ``rational&#39;&#39; case, where $C = \CC$.  We use a specific boundary condition at infinity: we consider multiplicative Higgs bundles on $\bb{CP}^1$ with a fixed framing at infinity.  In other words we study the moduli space $\mhiggs^{\text{fr}}_G(\bb{CP}^1,D,\omega^\vee)$ of multiplicative Higgs bundles on $\bb{CP}^1$ with prescribed singularities lying at the points $D = \{z_1, \ldots, z_k\}$, with local data at the singuarities encoded by $\omega_{z_1}^\vee, \ldots, \omega_{z_k}^\vee$ respectively, and with a fixed framing at $\infty$.  This moduli space is a smooth algebraic variety with dimension depending on the coweights we chose</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L183" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="183"></td>
        <td id="LC183" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L184" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="184"></td>
        <td id="LC184" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> In the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is Calabi-Yau the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles admits a one-parameter deformation; from the above point of view, the moduli space is hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler so we can rotate the complex structure within the twistor sphere.  The result of this deformation also has a natural interpretation in terms of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections}.  That is, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> equipped with an isomorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>^*P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and its translate by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can summarize this identification as follows.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L185" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="185"></td>
        <td id="LC185" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L186" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="186"></td>
        <td id="LC186" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem} [See Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{HK_rotation_thm}]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L187" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="187"></td>
        <td id="LC187" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> The moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr}}_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, given the complex structure at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the twistor sphere can be identified (in the limit where an auxiliary parameter is taken to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) with the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\epsconn</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr}}_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of framed <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L188" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="188"></td>
        <td id="LC188" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>

      <tr>
        <td id="L192" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="192"></td>
        <td id="LC192" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If we focus on the example where a real three-dimensional Riemannian</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC193" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">manifold <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M = C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> splits as the product of a compact Riemann</td>

      </tr>

        <td id="L197" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="197"></td>
        <td id="LC197" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">perspective of the Coulomb branch of vacua of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathcal</span>{N}=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>

        <td id="L198" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="198"></td>
        <td id="LC198" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">supersymmetric gauge theory. For general <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the moduli space of</td>

        <td id="L199" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="199"></td>
