      <tr>
        <td id="L200" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="200"></td>
        <td id="LC200" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Charbonneau--Hurtubise <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CharbonneauHurtubise}, for</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L201" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="201"></td>
        <td id="LC201" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span> U(n)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and by Smith <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Smith} for general <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  These</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L202" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="202"></td>
        <td id="LC202" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">moduli spaces were also studied in the rational case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L203" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="203"></td>
        <td id="LC203" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">with more general boundary conditions than the framing at infinity</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L204" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="204"></td>
        <td id="LC204" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which we consider.  This example has also been studied in the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L205" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="205"></td>
        <td id="LC205" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">mathematics literature by Foscolo <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FoscoloDef, FoscoloThesis} and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L206" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="206"></td>
        <td id="LC206" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">by Mochizuki <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Mochizuki} -- note that considering weaker boundary</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L207" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="207"></td>
        <td id="LC207" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">conditions at infinity means they need to use far more sophisticated</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L208" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="208"></td>
        <td id="LC208" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">analysis in order to work with hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structures on their</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L209" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="209"></td>
        <td id="LC209" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">moduli spaces than we&#39;ll consider in this paper.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L210" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="210"></td>
        <td id="LC210" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L211" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="211"></td>
        <td id="LC211" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The connection between periodic monopoles and multiplicative Higgs bundles is provided by the following theorem.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L212" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="212"></td>
        <td id="LC212" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem}[Charbonneau--Hurtubise, Smith]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L213" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="213"></td>
        <td id="LC213" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  There is an analytic isomorphism </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L214" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="214"></td>
        <td id="LC214" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{equation*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L215" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="215"></td>
        <td id="LC215" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    H: <span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1,D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span>0<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr}}(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L216" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="216"></td>
        <td id="LC216" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{equation*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L217" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="217"></td>
        <td id="LC217" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">between the moduli space of (polystable) multiplicative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs bundles on a compact curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with singularities at points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, z_k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and residues <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_1}, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_k}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the moduli space of periodic monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with Dirac singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>), <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, (z_k,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with charges <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_1}, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_k}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L218" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="218"></td>
        <td id="LC218" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L219" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="219"></td>
        <td id="LC219" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L220" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="220"></td>
        <td id="LC220" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The morphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>,  discussed first by Cherkis and Kapustin in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CherkisKapustin2} and later in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L221" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="221"></td>
        <td id="LC221" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CharbonneauHurtubise}, <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Smith}, <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L222" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="222"></td>
        <td id="LC222" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">defines the value of the multiplicative Higgs field at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be equal to</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L223" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="223"></td>
        <td id="LC223" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the holonomy of the monopole connection (complexified by the scalar field) along the fiber circle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span>z<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^{1} <span class="pl-c1">\subset</span> M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L224" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="224"></td>
        <td id="LC224" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L225" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="225"></td>
        <td id="LC225" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One of our main goals in this paper is to compare -- in the rational case -- the symplectic structure on the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs fields analogous to the symplectic structure defined by Hurtubise and Markman in the elliptic case, and the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure on the moduli space of periodic monopoles, defined by realizing the moduli space of periodic monopoles as a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler quotient.  We prove that they coincide.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L226" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="226"></td>
        <td id="LC226" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L227" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="227"></td>
        <td id="LC227" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem}[See Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{symplectic_comparison_thm}]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L228" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="228"></td>
        <td id="LC228" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  The holomorphic symplectic structure on</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L229" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="229"></td>
        <td id="LC229" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (at 0</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L230" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="230"></td>
        <td id="LC230" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  in the twistor sphere of holomorphic symplectic structures) </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L231" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="231"></td>
        <td id="LC231" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  is isomorphic to the pullback of the natural symplectic structure on</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L232" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="232"></td>
        <td id="LC232" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L233" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="233"></td>
        <td id="LC233" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  holonomy morphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L234" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="234"></td>
        <td id="LC234" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L235" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="235"></td>
        <td id="LC235" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L236" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="236"></td>
        <td id="LC236" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In particular, the symplectic structure on the multiplicative Higgs moduli space extends to a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure, as we discussed in point 1 above.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L237" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="237"></td>
        <td id="LC237" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L238" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="238"></td>
        <td id="LC238" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Poisson-Lie Groups}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L239" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="239"></td>
        <td id="LC239" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The third perspective that we&#39;ll consider connects our moduli spaces directly to the theory of Poisson Lie groups and Lie bialgebras, and leads to an interesting connection to quantum groups upon quantization.  By the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{rational Poisson Lie group} we&#39;ll mean the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consisting of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued power series in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with constant term <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More precisely this is an ind-algebraic group: it is expressed as a direct limit of algebraic varieties <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with an associative multiplication <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]_m <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]_n <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]_{m+n}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The Poisson structure on this group can be thought of as coming from a Manin triple: specifically the triple <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(G(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z^{-1})<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>), G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]], G[z])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is equipped with the residue pairing (see Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{quantization_section} for more details).  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L240" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="240"></td>
        <td id="LC240" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L241" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="241"></td>
        <td id="LC241" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We claim that our moduli spaces <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> correspond to <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{symplectic leaves} in the rational Poisson Lie group, extending a classification result of Shapiro <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Shapiro} for the groups <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More specifically, we prove the following.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L242" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="242"></td>
        <td id="LC242" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem}[See Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Poisson_Lie_Comparison_thm}]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L243" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="243"></td>
        <td id="LC243" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, defined by restricting a multiplicative Higgs field to a formal neighborhood of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, is Poisson.  That is, the pullback of the Poisson structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> coincides with the Poisson bracket on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L244" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="244"></td>
        <td id="LC244" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L245" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="245"></td>
        <td id="LC245" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L246" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="246"></td>
        <td id="LC246" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From this point of view it&#39;s natural to try to understand how our moduli spaces behave under deformation quantization.  The quantization of the rational Poisson Lie group is well known: it&#39;s modelled by the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Yangian} quantum group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  When we quantize our symplectic leaves, we obtain <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules.  This follows from the work of Gerasimov, Kharchev, Lebedev and Oblezin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GKLO} who constructed the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules in question and analyzed their classical limits.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L247" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="247"></td>
        <td id="LC247" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L248" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="248"></td>
        <td id="LC248" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L249" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="249"></td>
        <td id="LC249" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The article <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GKLO}, as well as its generalizations such as the work of Kamnitzer, Webster, Weekes and Yacobi <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KWWY}, view these <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules as quantizing certain moduli spaces of monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and not of monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  These two points of view are expected to be related in the limit where the radius of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is sent to infinity, with the positions of the singularities in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> kept fixed (note that while the holomorphic symplectic structure on the moduli space is independent of this radius, the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{will} be sensitive to it).  The moduli space of periodic monopoles in the rational case would in this limit be related to the moduli space of monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (perhaps with certain restrictions as in the work of Finkelberg, Kuznetsov and Rybnikov on trigonometric Zastava spaces <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FKR}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L250" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="250"></td>
        <td id="LC250" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L251" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="251"></td>
        <td id="LC251" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L252" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="252"></td>
        <td id="LC252" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Moduli Spaces in Supersymmetric Gauge Theory} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{intro_gauge_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L253" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="253"></td>
        <td id="LC253" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Having discussed three points of view on our moduli space in geometric representation theory, let us move on to explain some of the ways in which multiplicative Higgs bundles / periodic monopoles arise naturally in the world of supersymmetric gauge theory.  The general program relating supersymmetric gauge theory and quantum integrable systems relevant for the present work arose from the work of Nekrasov and Shatashvili in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Nekrasov:2009ui,Nekrasov:2009rc}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L254" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="254"></td>
        <td id="LC254" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L255" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="255"></td>
        <td id="LC255" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Concretely, the moduli spaces of periodic monopoles (and implicitly its quantization) appeared in work of the second author, Nekrasov and Shatashvili <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun, NekrasovPestunShatashvili} concerning the Seiberg-Witten integrable systems of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> ADE quiver gauge theories.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a simple Lie algebra of ADE type.  One can define an <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> superconformal 4d gauge theory modelled on the Dynkin diagram of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  To define this theory one must specify masses <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m_{i,j}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for fundamental hypermultiplets associated to the vertices of the Dynkin diagram, so <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i = <span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> varies over the vertices of the Dynkin diagram and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j=<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,w_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an index parameterizing the number of hypermultiplets at each vertex.  Let us assume we&#39;re in the generic situation, where the masses are all distinct.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L256" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="256"></td>
        <td id="LC256" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L257" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="257"></td>
        <td id="LC257" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The paper <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun} studied the Seiberg-Witten integrable system associated to this theory, so in particular the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the Coulomb branch of the moduli space of vacua,  occuring as the target of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> supersymmetric sigma model obtained by compactifying the 4d theory on a circle.  In particular, it proved the following.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L258" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="258"></td>
        <td id="LC258" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L259" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="259"></td>
        <td id="LC259" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem}[{<span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 8.1]{NekrasovPestun}}]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L260" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="260"></td>
        <td id="LC260" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a simple Lie group with ADE Lie algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The phase space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is isomorphic, as a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler manifold, to the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of periodic monopoles, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>m_{i,j}<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and where the residue <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{m_{i,j}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the fundamental coweight corresponding to the vertex <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the Dynkin diagram of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L261" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="261"></td>
        <td id="LC261" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L262" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="262"></td>
        <td id="LC262" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L263" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="263"></td>
        <td id="LC263" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L264" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="264"></td>
        <td id="LC264" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If one considers gauge theories that are not necessarily conformal, but only asymptotically free, the phase space is modelled by periodic monopoles that are permitted to have a singularity at infinity.  If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\SU</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> then this moduli space fits into the framework studied by Cherkis--Kapustin and by Foscolo.  We won&#39;t discuss this more complicated setting further in this paper.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L265" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="265"></td>
        <td id="LC265" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L266" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="266"></td>
        <td id="LC266" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L267" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="267"></td>
        <td id="LC267" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}[Elliptic fiber version]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L268" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="268"></td>
        <td id="LC268" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  The analysis of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun} suggests an elliptic fiber</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L269" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="269"></td>
        <td id="LC269" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  generalization of our multiplicative story, corresponding to the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L270" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="270"></td>
        <td id="LC270" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  phase space of a theory modelled on an <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{affine} ADE quiver.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L271" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="271"></td>
        <td id="LC271" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  The phase space of these theories is identified with a moduli space</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L272" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="272"></td>
        <td id="LC272" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  of doubly periodic instantons.  In our setting, the idea is the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L273" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="273"></td>
        <td id="LC273" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  following.  We can think of the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L274" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="274"></td>
        <td id="LC274" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  bundles as a moduli space of meromorphic functions into the adjoint</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L275" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="275"></td>
        <td id="LC275" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  quotient stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, just like we can think of the moduli space of</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L276" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="276"></td>
        <td id="LC276" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  ordinary Higgs bundles as a moduli space of meromorphic functions</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L277" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="277"></td>
        <td id="LC277" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  into the adjoint quotient stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the Lie algebra.  There</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L278" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="278"></td>
        <td id="LC278" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  is a rational/trigonometric/elliptic trichotomy extending these two</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L279" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="279"></td>
        <td id="LC279" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  examples: one studies the moduli stack of semistable <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L280" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="280"></td>
        <td id="LC280" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  a cuspidal, nodal or smooth elliptic curve.  That is:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L281" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="281"></td>
        <td id="LC281" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L282" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="282"></td>
        <td id="LC282" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ss}}_G(E^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{cusp}}) &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>/G <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L283" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="283"></td>
        <td id="LC283" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ss}}_G(E^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{nod}}) &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> G/G <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L284" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="284"></td>
        <td id="LC284" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ss}}_G(E_q) &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> LG/_q LG.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L285" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="285"></td>
        <td id="LC285" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L286" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="286"></td>
        <td id="LC286" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The last statement is a theorem of Looijenga (see e.g. <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Laszlo}): <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>LG/_q LG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> denotes the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted adjoint quotient of the loop group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>LG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: so <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> acts by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>h(z) <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> g(qz)^{-1}h(z)g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L287" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="287"></td>
        <td id="LC287" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L288" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="288"></td>
        <td id="LC288" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Without singularities, therefore, the elliptic analogue of our</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L289" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="289"></td>
        <td id="LC289" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">multiplicative Hitchin system should be the space of maps from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L290" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="290"></td>
        <td id="LC290" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">into <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ss}}_G(E_q)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: this moduli space is closely related to</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L291" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="291"></td>
        <td id="LC291" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">the moduli space of instantons on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> E_q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. doubly periodic</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L292" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="292"></td>
        <td id="LC292" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">instantons.  It would be interesting to study this elliptic Hitchin</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L293" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="293"></td>
        <td id="LC293" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">system in the full, singular setting.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L294" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="294"></td>
        <td id="LC294" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L295" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="295"></td>
        <td id="LC295" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L296" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="296"></td>
        <td id="LC296" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Multiplicative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Geometric Langlands Correspondence}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L297" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="297"></td>
        <td id="LC297" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The final perspective we&#39;ll consider is perhaps the most interesting from our point of view, because it suggests that the categorical geometric Langlands conjecture of Beilinson and Drinfeld might admit a multiplicative analogue, built from the multiplicative Hitchin system instead of the ordinary Hitchin system.  Again, we&#39;ll describe a moduli space coming from supersymmetric gauge theory, but in a quite different setting to that of perspective 4 above.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L298" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="298"></td>
        <td id="LC298" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L299" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="299"></td>
        <td id="LC299" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We consider now a five-dimensional <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> supersymmetric gauge theory.  In order to extract interesting moduli spaces for geometric representation theory, we won&#39;t study its moduli space of vacua, but instead we&#39;ll <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{twist} the theory, then look at the entire moduli space of solutions to the equations of motion in the twisted theory.  We&#39;ll review the idea behind twisting at the beginning of Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{twist_section}, but very informally, we&#39;ll choose a supersymmetry <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that squares to zero, and study the derived space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-invariant solutions to the equations of motion.  In Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{twist_section} we&#39;ll sketch the following, which also follows from forthcoming work of Butson <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Butson}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L300" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="300"></td>
        <td id="LC300" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L301" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="301"></td>
        <td id="LC301" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{claimnum}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L302" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="302"></td>
        <td id="LC302" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The twist by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory with gauge group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, on the 5-manifold <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a Calabi-Yau curve,and  with monopole surface operators placed at the points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>), <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, (z_k,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with charges <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_1}, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_k}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> respectively, has the following stack of solutions to the equations of motion:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L303" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="303"></td>
        <td id="LC303" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{EOM}(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^2) = T^*[1]<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L304" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="304"></td>
        <td id="LC304" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T^*[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> denotes the ``1-shifted cotangent space&#39;&#39; of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L305" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="305"></td>
        <td id="LC305" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{claimnum}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L306" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="306"></td>
        <td id="LC306" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L307" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="307"></td>
        <td id="LC307" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This story leads us to a ``multiplicative&#39;&#39; analogue of the approach to geometric Langlands introduced by Kapustin and Witten <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KapustinWitten}.  When we take the radius of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to zero we recover Kapustin&#39;s partially topological twist <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KapustinHolo} of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills, which degenerates to Kapustin-Witten&#39;s A- and B-topologically twisted theories.  By ``multiplicative geometric Langlands&#39;&#39; we mean a version of the geometric Langlands conjecture modelled on the multiplicative Hitchin system instead of the ordinary Hitchin system, where the radius of this circle is kept positive.  For more details on what this means, see Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Langlands_section}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L308" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="308"></td>
        <td id="LC308" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L309" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="309"></td>
        <td id="LC309" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}[Derived geometry]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L310" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="310"></td>
        <td id="LC310" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  We&#39;ll use the language of derived algebraic geometry in several places in this paper, mainly in Sections \ref{mhiggs_def_section} and \ref{twist_section}.  While we believe this perspective provides a clear way of thinking about the moduli spaces we&#39;re interested in studying, the derived language is not necessary when we state and prove the main results of this paper.  We hope that the majority of the paper is understandable without a derived geometry background.  There are several clear and references explaining the point of view of derived algebraic geometry, for instance the survey articles of To\&quot;en \cite{ToenOverview,ToenSurvey}.  A comprehensive account of the theory of derived geometry can be found in the book of Gaitsgory and Rozenblyum \cite{GRvol1, GRvol2}.  We&#39;ll also refer a few times to the theory of shifted symplectic structures.  This theory was developed by Pantev, To\&quot;en, Vaqui\&#39;e and Vezzosi \cite{PTVV}, and we also recommend the explanations in \cite{Calaque}.  From the physical point of view, the ideas of derived geometry appear in classical field theory through the Batalin-Vilkovisky formalism, and through Pantev, To\&quot;en, Vaqui\&#39;e and Vezzosi&#39;s derived version of the AKSZ construction of symplectic structures on mapping spaces \cite{AKSZ}. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L311" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="311"></td>
        <td id="LC311" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L312" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="312"></td>
        <td id="LC312" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L313" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="313"></td>
        <td id="LC313" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Outline of the Paper}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L314" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="314"></td>
        <td id="LC314" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We begin in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{mhiggs_def_section} by introducing and defining the moduli spaces we&#39;ll be studying in this paper: the moduli spaces of multiplicative Higgs bundles.  We discuss the trichotomy of rational, trigonometric and elliptic examples that are most relevant to us: where the moduli space has the structure of an integrable system.  We include a discussion of how the symplectic structures we&#39;re studying in this paper are expected to arise from the theory of derived symplectic geometry.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L315" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="315"></td>
        <td id="LC315" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L316" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="316"></td>
        <td id="LC316" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The following section, Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{twist_section}, stands alone from the rest of the paper.  In this section we explain how the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles appears when one studies a certain partially topological twist of 5d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> supersymmetric gauge theory.  As a consequence, we can speculate on the existence of a multiplicative version of the geometric Langlands conjecture, using the work of Kapustin and Witten.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L317" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="317"></td>
        <td id="LC317" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L318" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="318"></td>
        <td id="LC318" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{periodic_monopole_section} we discuss the moduli space of periodic monopoles and its identification with the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles.  We describe the tangent space to the moduli space from both points of view, which we&#39;ll then use in the following section, Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{symp_section}.  Here we prove our main result, identifying the symplectic structures on the moduli spaces of periodic monopoles and on multiplicative Higgs bundles.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L319" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="319"></td>
        <td id="LC319" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L320" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="320"></td>
        <td id="LC320" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Having done this, in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{hyperkahler_section} we can transfer the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure on the moduli space of periodic monopoles across to the multiplicative Hitchin system.  The main thing we can do is to identify the twistor rotation on this moduli space: after rotating to a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the twistor sphere we identify the holomorphic symplectic moduli space with the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference connections, i.e. <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with an isomorphism between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and its translate by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L321" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="321"></td>
        <td id="LC321" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L322" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="322"></td>
        <td id="LC322" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{quantization_section} we discuss the quantization of our moduli spaces.  We identify the moduli spaces of multiplicative Higgs bundles with symplectic leaves in the rational Poisson Lie group, and then after quantization we identify the quantized algebra of functions on our moduli spaces with modules for the Yangian as first constructed by Gerasimov, Kharchev, Lebedev and Oblezin. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L323" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="323"></td>
        <td id="LC323" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L324" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="324"></td>
        <td id="LC324" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{qchar_section} we discuss the relationship between the multiplicative analogue of the space of opers and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-character, motivated by the origin of the multiplicative Hitchin system in quiver gauge theory.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L325" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="325"></td>
        <td id="LC325" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L326" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="326"></td>
        <td id="LC326" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The preliminary results of this work were announced by the second author at String-Math 2017 <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{PestunStringMath}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L327" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="327"></td>
        <td id="LC327" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L328" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="328"></td>
        <td id="LC328" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Acknowledgements}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L329" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="329"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L330" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="330"></td>
        <td id="LC330" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L331" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="331"></td>
        <td id="LC331" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Multiplicative Higgs Bundles and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Connections} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{mhiggs_def_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L332" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="332"></td>
        <td id="LC332" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll begin with an abstract definition of moduli spaces of multiplicative Higgs bundles using the language of derived algebraic geometry.  We note, however, that once we specialize to our main, rational, example, the moduli spaces we&#39;ll end up studying are actually smooth algebraic varieties, not derived stacks.  However, the derived point of view gives us a useful and concise definition of these moduli spaces in full generality.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L333" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="333"></td>
        <td id="LC333" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L334" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="334"></td>
        <td id="LC334" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a reductive complex algebraic group, let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a smooth complex algebraic curve and fix a finite set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>z_i, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, z_k<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of closed points in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the moduli stack of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which we view as a mapping stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C, BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> into the classifying stack of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L335" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="335"></td>
        <td id="LC335" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L336" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="336"></td>
        <td id="LC336" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L337" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="337"></td>
        <td id="LC337" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The moduli stack of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{multiplicative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs fields} on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the fiber product</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L338" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="338"></td>
        <td id="LC338" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D) = <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)} <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D, G/G)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L339" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="339"></td>
        <td id="LC339" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the adjoint quotient stack.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L340" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="340"></td>
        <td id="LC340" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L341" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="341"></td>
        <td id="LC341" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L342" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="342"></td>
        <td id="LC342" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L343" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="343"></td>
        <td id="LC343" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A closed point of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consists of a principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along with an automorphism of the restriction <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P|_{C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. a section of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> away from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L344" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="344"></td>
        <td id="LC344" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L345" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="345"></td>
        <td id="LC345" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L346" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="346"></td>
        <td id="LC346" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The adjoint quotient stack can also be described as the derived loop space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B, BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the classifying stack, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the ``Betti stack&#39;&#39; of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. the constant derived stack at the simplicial set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can therefore view <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D, G/G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> instead as the mapping stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>((C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B, BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the moduli stack of multiplicative Higgs bundles instead as</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L347" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="347"></td>
        <td id="LC347" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D) = <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>((C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1_B) <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>0<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>), BG).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span>  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L348" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="348"></td>
        <td id="LC348" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The source of this mapping stack can be <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-deformed.  Indeed, let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> denote an automorphism of the curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{mapping torus} of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e the derived fiber product</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L349" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="349"></td>
        <td id="LC349" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^1_B = C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> C} C<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L350" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="350"></td>
        <td id="LC350" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the two maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are given by the diagonal and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted diagonal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> (x,q(x))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> respectively.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L351" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="351"></td>
        <td id="LC351" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L352" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="352"></td>

        <td id="L353" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="353"></td>
        <td id="LC353" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The moduli stack of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference connections} for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the mapping space</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L354" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="354"></td>
        <td id="LC354" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D) = <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>((C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^1_B) <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>0<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>), BG).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span> </td>

        <td id="L367" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="367"></td>
        <td id="LC367" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Local Conditions at the Singurities}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L368" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="368"></td>
        <td id="LC368" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">These moduli stacks are typically of infinite type.  In order to obtain finite type stacks, and later in order to define symplectic rather than only Poisson structures, we can fix the behaviour of our multiplicative Higgs fields and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference connections near the punctures <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L369" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="369"></td>
        <td id="LC369" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L370" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="370"></td>
        <td id="LC370" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to denote the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{formal disk} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\spec</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>[[z]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Likewise we&#39;ll write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{formal punctured disk} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\spec</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We&#39;ll then write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the derived pushout <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D <span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>LG = <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>, G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^+G = <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D, G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L371" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="371"></td>
        <td id="LC371" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L372" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="372"></td>
        <td id="LC372" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is a canonical inclusion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B^{<span class="pl-c1">\sqcup</span> k} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> (C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B) <span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the inclusion of the formal punctured neighborhood of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This induces a restriction map on mapping spaces</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L373" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="373"></td>
        <td id="LC373" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\res</span>_D <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C, D) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)^k.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>

</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L375" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="375"></td>
        <td id="LC375" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One can identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the double quotient stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^+G <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> LG / L^+G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or equivalently with the quotient <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^+G <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the affine Grassmannian.  The following is well-known (see e.g. the expository article <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Zhu}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L376" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="376"></td>
        <td id="LC376" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>

        <td id="L378" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="378"></td>
        <td id="LC378" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The set of closed points of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in canonical bijection with the set of dominant coweights of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>

        <td id="L381" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="381"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L382" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="382"></td>
        <td id="LC382" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Choose a map from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the set of dominant coweights and denote it by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> z_i <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the isotropy group of the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The moduli stack of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> difference connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and fixed local data given by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is defined to be the fiber product</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L383" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="383"></td>
        <td id="LC383" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)^k} (B<span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>_1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cdots</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> B<span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>_k).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L384" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="384"></td>
        <td id="LC384" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L385" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="385"></td>

</td>
