        <td id="L386" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="386"></td>
        <td id="LC386" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}<span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{ind_structure_remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L387" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="387"></td>
        <td id="LC387" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  In a similar way we can define a filtration on the moduli stack of</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L388" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="388"></td>
        <td id="LC388" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections.  Recall that the affine Grassmannian <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L389" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="389"></td>
        <td id="LC389" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  stratified by dominant coweights <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and there is an</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L390" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="390"></td>
        <td id="LC390" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  inclusion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_1}<span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_2}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L391" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="391"></td>
        <td id="LC391" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  one stratum into the closure of another stratum if and only if</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L392" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="392"></td>
        <td id="LC392" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\preceq</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with respect to the standard</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L393" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="393"></td>
        <td id="LC393" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  partial order on dominant coweights (again, this is explained in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Zhu}).  We can then define</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L394" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="394"></td>
        <td id="LC394" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D, <span class="pl-c1">\preceq</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)^k} <span class="pl-c1">\left</span>(L^+G <span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_1}} <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cdots</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> L^+G <span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\Gr</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_k}}<span class="pl-c1">\right</span>).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L395" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="395"></td>
        <td id="LC395" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The full moduli stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the filtered colimit of these moduli spaces.  One can additionally take the filtered colimit over all finite subsets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in order to define a moduli stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{sing}_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with arbitrary singularities.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L396" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="396"></td>
        <td id="LC396" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>

      <tr>
        <td id="L398" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="398"></td>
        <td id="LC398" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{examples}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L399" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="399"></td>
        <td id="LC399" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The most important examples for our purposes are given by the following rational/trigonometric/elliptic trichotomy.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L400" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="400"></td>
        <td id="LC400" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L401" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="401"></td>
        <td id="LC401" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> <span class="pl-c1">\textbf</span>{Rational:} We can enhance the definition of our moduli space by including a framing at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> not contained in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We always assume that such framed points are fixed by the automorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L402" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="402"></td>
        <td id="LC402" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L403" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="403"></td>
        <td id="LC403" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">      <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{def:framing}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L404" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="404"></td>
        <td id="LC404" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    The moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is defined to be the relative mapping space </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L405" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="405"></td>
        <td id="LC405" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(C) = <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^1_B, BG; f)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L406" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="406"></td>
        <td id="LC406" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (or equivalently <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) is a choice of adjoint orbit.  We can define the framed mapping space with singularities and fixed local data in exactly the same way as above.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L407" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="407"></td>
        <td id="LC407" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L408" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="408"></td>
        <td id="LC408" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L409" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="409"></td>
        <td id="LC409" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  In this paper we&#39;ll be most interested in the following example.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with framing point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c = <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and framing given by a fixed element in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and consider automorphisms of the form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> z + <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Choose a finite subset <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and label the points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by dominant coweights <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can then study the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\epsconn</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The main object of study in this paper will be the holomorphic symplectic structure on this moduli space. Note that the motivation for this definition comes in part from</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L410" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="410"></td>
        <td id="LC410" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    Spaide&#39;s formalism <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Spaide} of AKSZ-type derived symplectic structures (in the sense of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{AKSZ,PTVV}) on</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L411" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="411"></td>
        <td id="LC411" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    relative mapping spaces -- in this formalism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a single framing point is relatively 1-oriented, so mapping spaces</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L412" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="412"></td>
        <td id="LC412" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    out of it with 1-shifted symplectic targets have AKSZ 0-shifted symplectic structures.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L413" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="413"></td>
        <td id="LC413" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L414" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="414"></td>
        <td id="LC414" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> <span class="pl-c1">\textbf</span>{Trigonometric:} Alternatively, we can enhance our definition by including a reduction of structure group at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> not contained in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, again fixed by the automorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L415" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="415"></td>
        <td id="LC415" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L416" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="416"></td>
        <td id="LC416" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   The moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with an <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-reduction at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for a subgroup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is defined to be the fiber product</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L417" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="417"></td>
        <td id="LC417" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   <span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G^{H,c}(C) = <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^1_B,BG) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{G/G} H/H<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L418" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="418"></td>
        <td id="LC418" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   associated to the evaluation at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B,BG) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can define the moduli space with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-reduction with singularities and fixed local data in the same way as above.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L419" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="419"></td>
        <td id="LC419" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L420" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="420"></td>
        <td id="LC420" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L421" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="421"></td>
        <td id="LC421" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  Again let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Fix a pair of opposite Borel subgroups <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_+<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_- <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with unipotent radicals <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>N_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and consider the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_+<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-reduction at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>N_-<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-reduction at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We&#39;ll now take <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be an automorphism of the form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> qz<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We&#39;ll defer in depth analysis of this example to future work.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L422" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="422"></td>
        <td id="LC422" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L423" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="423"></td>
        <td id="LC423" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> <span class="pl-c1">\textbf</span>{Elliptic:} Finally, let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = E<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a smooth curve of genus one.  In this case we won&#39;t fix any additional boundary data, but just consider the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(E,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In the case <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q = <span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> this space -- or rather its polystable locus -- was studied by Hurtubise and Markman <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{HurtubiseMarkman}, who proved that it can be given the structure of an algebraic integrable system with symplectic structure related to the elliptic R-matrix of Etingof and Varchenko <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{EtingofVarchenko}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L424" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="424"></td>
        <td id="LC424" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L425" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="425"></td>
        <td id="LC425" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{examples}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L426" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="426"></td>
        <td id="LC426" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L427" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="427"></td>
        <td id="LC427" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L428" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="428"></td>
        <td id="LC428" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the rational case, the moduli space of framed <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference connections now depends on a new parameter: the value of the framing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  From the point of view of the ADE quiver gauge theory, as in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{intro_gauge_section}, this value -- or rather its image in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- corresponds to the value of the gauge coupling constants in the quiver gauge theory.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L429" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="429"></td>
        <td id="LC429" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L430" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="430"></td>
        <td id="LC430" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L431" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="431"></td>
        <td id="LC431" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Elliptic_AKSZ_remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L432" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="432"></td>
        <td id="LC432" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the elliptic case it&#39;s natural to ask to what extent Hurtubise and Markman&#39;s integrable system structure can be extended from the variety of polystable multiplicative Higgs bundles to the full moduli stack.  If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is empty then it&#39;s easy to see that we have a symplectic structure given by the AKSZ construction of Pantev-To<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>en-Vaqui<span class="pl-cce">\&#39;</span>e-Vezzosi <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{PTVV}.  Indeed, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is compact 1-oriented and the quotient stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted symplectic, so the mapping stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(E, G/G) = <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(E)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is equipped with a 0-shifted symplectic structure by <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Theorem 2.5]{PTVV}.  The role of the Hitchin fibration is played by the Chevalley map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> G/G <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and therefore</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L433" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="433"></td>
        <td id="LC433" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(E,G/G) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(E,T/W).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L434" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="434"></td>
        <td id="LC434" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The fibers of this map over regular points in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are given by moduli stacks of the form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_T(<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> E)^W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> E<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-fold cover of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (the cameral cover).  Note that in this unramified case the curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> E<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> also has genus 1; counting dimensions we see that the base has dimension <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r = <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{rk}(G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the generic fibers are <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-dimensional (Lagrangian) tori.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L435" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="435"></td>
        <td id="LC435" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L436" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="436"></td>
        <td id="LC436" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L437" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="437"></td>
        <td id="LC437" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L438" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="438"></td>
        <td id="LC438" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">While the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles makes sense on a general curve it&#39;s only after restricting attention to this trichotomy of examples that we&#39;ll expect the existence of a Poisson structure.  In the non-singular case, such a structure arises by the AKSZ construction, i.e. by transgressing the 1-shifted symplectic structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the mapping space using a fixed section of the canonical bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (possibly with a boundary condition).  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L439" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="439"></td>
        <td id="LC439" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L440" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="440"></td>
        <td id="LC440" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L441" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="441"></td>
        <td id="LC441" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{The Multiplicative Hitchin System} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Hitchin_system_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L442" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="442"></td>
        <td id="LC442" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can define the global Chevalley map as in Remark <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Elliptic_AKSZ_remark} in the case of non-empty <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as well.  We&#39;ll show that in the rational case this defines a completely integrable system structure.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a maximal torus, and write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the Weyl group of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L443" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="443"></td>
        <td id="LC443" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L444" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="444"></td>
        <td id="LC444" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{mult_Hitchin_system_def}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L445" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="445"></td>
        <td id="LC445" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Fix a curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, a divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a dominant coweight <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{z_i}^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at each point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{multiplicative Hitchin base} is the stack</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L446" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="446"></td>
        <td id="LC446" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Sect}(C, X(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)/W)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L447" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="447"></td>
        <td id="LC447" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of sections of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle characterized by the condition that the associated line bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_T {<span class="pl-c1">\lambda</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> corresponding to a weight <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\lambda</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\sum</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{z_i}^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\lambda</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\cdot</span> z_i)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (c.f. <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 3.3]{HurtubiseMarkman}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L448" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="448"></td>
        <td id="LC448" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L449" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="449"></td>
        <td id="LC449" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{multiplicative Hitchin fibration} is the map</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L450" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="450"></td>
        <td id="LC450" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L451" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="451"></td>
        <td id="LC451" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">given by post-composing a map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the Chevalley map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> G/G <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L452" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="452"></td>
        <td id="LC452" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L453" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="453"></td>
        <td id="LC453" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L454" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="454"></td>
        <td id="LC454" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L455" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="455"></td>
        <td id="LC455" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The multiplicative Hitchin fibration described above is well-defined.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L456" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="456"></td>
        <td id="LC456" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L457" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="457"></td>
        <td id="LC457" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L458" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="458"></td>
        <td id="LC458" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L459" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="459"></td>
        <td id="LC459" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We need to verify that the image of a point in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, viewed as a section of the trivial <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, extends to a section of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We look locally near a singularity <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\phi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G((z_i))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a local representative for a multiplicative Higgs field in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. an element of the associated <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G[[z_i]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-adjoint orbit.  Since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is equivalent to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i^{-<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the action of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G[[z_i]]^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by left and right multiplication, without loss of generality we can say that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\phi</span> = z_i^{-<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}} <span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for some <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G[[z_i]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Consider <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> T((z_i))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- the singular part of this element is the same as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>(z_i^{-<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}} g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for some <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which implies the section extends to a meromorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued function of the required type.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L460" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="460"></td>
        <td id="LC460" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L461" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="461"></td>
        <td id="LC461" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L462" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="462"></td>
        <td id="LC462" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L463" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="463"></td>
        <td id="LC463" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Note that the base stack that we&#39;re defining here is not exactly the same as the base of the integrable system defined in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{HurtubiseMarkman}.  The difference comes from the way in which we treat the Weyl group quotient; the Hurtubise-Markman base is an algebraic variety defined essentially by taking the part of our space of sections where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> acts freely as an open subset, then constructing a compactification using techniques from toric geometry.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L464" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="464"></td>
        <td id="LC464" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L465" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="465"></td>
        <td id="LC465" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L466" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="466"></td>
        <td id="LC466" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll show in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{general_symplectic_sec} that this fibration defines a completely integrable system in the rational case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More specifically, we&#39;ll describe a non-degenerate pairing on the tangent space of the multiplicative Higgs moduli space, and in Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Hitchin_isotropic_prop} we&#39;ll show that the multiplicative Hitchin fibers are isotropic for this pairing.  Then, by comparison to the symplectic structure on periodic monopoles, we&#39;ll see that the pairing was symplectic.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L467" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="467"></td>
        <td id="LC467" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L468" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="468"></td>
        <td id="LC468" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here, we&#39;ll first observe that the generic fibers are half-dimensional tori, which will ultimately imply that the multiplicative Hitchin system is generically a Lagrangian fibration.  Computing the fibers of the Hitchin fibration works similarly to the non-singular case: a point in the base is, in particular, a map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Suppose this map lands in the regular locus <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{reg}}/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, then an element of the fiber over this point defines, in particular, a map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BT/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We would like to argue that the fiber consists of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on the cameral cover <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-fold cover of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> ramified at the divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L469" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="469"></td>
        <td id="LC469" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L470" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="470"></td>
        <td id="LC470" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to say this a bit more precisely this we&#39;ll compare our moduli space with the space of abstract Higgs bundles introduced by Donagi and Gaitsgory <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{DonagiGaitsgory} (see also <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{DonagiLectures}, where Donagi proposed the applicability of this abstract Higgs theory to the multiplicative situation and asked for a geometric interpretation).  Our argument will follow the same ideas as the arguments of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 6]{HurtubiseMarkman}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L471" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="471"></td>
        <td id="LC471" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L472" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="472"></td>
        <td id="LC472" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L473" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="473"></td>
        <td id="LC473" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">An <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{abstract <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs bundle} on a curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along with a sub-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{regular centralizers}, meaning that the fibers are subalgebras of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which arise as the centralizer of a regular element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{abs}}(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the moduli stack of abstract <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs bundles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L474" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="474"></td>
        <td id="LC474" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L475" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="475"></td>
        <td id="LC475" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L476" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="476"></td>
        <td id="LC476" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There&#39;s an algebraic map from the regular part of our moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{reg}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (where the Higgs field is required to take regular values) into <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{abs}}(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that sends a multiplicative Higgs bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the abstract Higgs bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P, <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> c_g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> c_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the sub-bundle of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fixed by the adjoint action of the multiplicative Higgs field <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  What&#39;s more, there is a commutative square relating the Hitchin fibration for the multiplicative moduli space with a related projection for the abstract moduli stack:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L477" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="477"></td>
        <td id="LC477" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\xymatrix</span>{</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L478" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="478"></td>
        <td id="LC478" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{reg}} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r] <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d] &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{abs}}(C) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d] <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L479" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="479"></td>
        <td id="LC479" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{reg}} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r] &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Cam}_G(C),</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L480" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="480"></td>
        <td id="LC480" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L481" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="481"></td>
        <td id="LC481" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Cam}_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the stack of cameral covers of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, as defined in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 2.8]{DonagiGaitsgory}.  The map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{reg}} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Cam}_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is defined by sending a meromorphic function <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> C <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-ramified cameral cover <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> C = C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{T/W} T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In particular there&#39;s a map from the multiplicative Hitchin fiber to the corresponding Donagi-Gaitsgory fiber: the moduli space of abstract <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs bundles with fixed cameral cover.  This map is surjective: having fixed the cameral cover, and therefore the ramification data, every sub-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> c <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of regular centralizers arises as the centralizer of some regular multiplicative Higgs field.  Likewise once one restricts to a single generic multiplicative Hitchin fiber the map is an unramified <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-fold cover.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L482" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="482"></td>
        <td id="LC482" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L483" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="483"></td>
        <td id="LC483" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To conclude this discussion we&#39;ll discuss dimensions and the geometry of the multiplicative Hitchin fibers.  Firstly, we can compute the dimension of a regular multiplicative Hitchin fiber by computing the dimension of the base and the dimension of the total space.  The dimension of the base is given by computing the number of linearly independent sections of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> vanishing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This is given by </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L484" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="484"></td>
        <td id="LC484" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\dim</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{z_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D} <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i} <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L485" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="485"></td>
        <td id="LC485" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\rho</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the Weyl vector.  On the other hand the dimension of the total space is calculated in Corollary <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{dim_of_moduli_space_cor} to be <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{z_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D} <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i} <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The base is indeed half-dimensional, therefore so is the fiber.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L486" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="486"></td>
        <td id="LC486" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L487" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="487"></td>
        <td id="LC487" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The Donagi-Gaitsgory fiber is, according to the main theorem of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{DonagiGaitsgory}, equivalent to the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-equivariant <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on the cameral curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> up to a discrete correction involving the root datum of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In particular it is generically an abelian variety.  The multiplicative Hitchin fiber is isogenous to this abelian variety, since the map from the multiplicative Hitchin fiber to the Donagi-Gaitsgory fiber is surjective and <span class="pl-cce">\&#39;</span>etale.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L488" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="488"></td>
        <td id="LC488" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L489" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="489"></td>
        <td id="LC489" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{q_opers_remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L490" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="490"></td>
        <td id="LC490" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Like in the case of the ordinary Hitchin system, in good examples the multiplicative Hitchin system admits a canonical Hitchin section.  One can construct this section using the Steinberg section (the multiplicative analogue of the Kostant section) \cite{Steinberg}.  This is a section of the map $G/G \to T/W$, canonical after choosing a Borel subgroup $B$ with maximal torus $T$ and a basis vector for each simple root space, and well defined as long as $G$ is simply connected \footnote{By a theorem of Popov \cite{Popov} this condition is necessary for semisimple $G$.  A section also exists for $G = \GL_n$, but we aren&#39;t aware of a necessary and sufficient condition for general reductive groups.}.  The \emph{multiplicative Hitchin section} is the map $\sigma \colon \mc B(C,D,\omega^\vee) \to \mhiggs_G(C,D,\omega^\vee)$ defined by post-composition with the Steinberg section.  One can use this section to define the moduli space of \emph{$q$-opers} for the group $G$ and the curve $\bb{CP}^1$ with its framing at infinity.  We&#39;ll discuss the hyperk\&quot;ahler structure on the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles in Section \ref{hyperkahler_section}.  In particular we&#39;ll show that when one rotates to $q$ in the twistor sphere one obtains the moduli space of $q$-connections on $\bb{CP}^1$.  The moduli space of $q$-opers is defined to be the Hitchin section, but viewed as a subspace of $\qconn^{\fr}_G(\bb{CP}^1,D,\omega^\vee)$.  For a more detailed discussion of the multiplicative Hitchin section and $q$-opers see Section \ref{qchar_section}. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L491" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="491"></td>
        <td id="LC491" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L492" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="492"></td>
        <td id="LC492" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L493" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="493"></td>
        <td id="LC493" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Stability Conditions}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L494" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="494"></td>
        <td id="LC494" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For comparison to results in the literature it is important that we briefly discuss the role of stability conditions for difference connections.  In our main example of interest -- the rational case -- these conditions won&#39;t play a role, but they do appear in the comparison results between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections and monopoles in the literature for more general curves.  For definitions for general <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we refer to <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Smith}, although see also <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{AnchoucheBiswas} on polystable <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles.  In what follows we fix a choice of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span> &lt; t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> &lt; <span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L495" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="495"></td>
        <td id="LC495" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L496" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="496"></td>
        <td id="LC496" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L497" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="497"></td>
        <td id="LC497" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection on a curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a character of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-degree} of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is defined to be </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L498" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="498"></td>
        <td id="LC498" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\deg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>(P,g) = <span class="pl-c1">\deg</span>(P <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) - <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {t_0}{2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R} <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^k <span class="pl-c1">\deg</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L499" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="499"></td>
        <td id="LC499" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L500" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="500"></td>
        <td id="LC500" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{stable} if for every maximal parabolic subgroup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with Levi decomposition <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H = LN<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and every reduction of structure group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P_H, g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we have</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L501" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="501"></td>
        <td id="LC501" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\deg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>(P_H, g) &lt; 0<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L502" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="502"></td>
        <td id="LC502" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for the character <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\det</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_L^{<span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> n})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defined to be the determinant of the adjoint representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L503" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="503"></td>
        <td id="LC503" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L504" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="504"></td>
        <td id="LC504" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{polystable} if there exists a (not necessarily maximal) parabolic subgroup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with Levi factor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a reduction of structure group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P_L, g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> so that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P_L,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a stable <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection and so that the associated <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle is admissible, meaning that for every character <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which is trivial on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Z(G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the associated line bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P_H <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has degree zero. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L505" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="505"></td>
        <td id="LC505" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L506" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="506"></td>
        <td id="LC506" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L507" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="507"></td>
        <td id="LC507" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Below we&#39;ll write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps}}(C, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the moduli space of polystable <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections.  This moduli space is a smooth algebraic variety of finite type.  If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the identity this is a theorem of Charbonneau, Hurtubise and Smith.  For more general <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, as a smooth manifold these moduli spaces are actually independent when one varies <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- we&#39;ll see this when we describe an equivalent description of these moduli spaces as spaces of periodic monopoles on diffeomorphic manifolds.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L508" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="508"></td>
        <td id="LC508" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L509" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="509"></td>
        <td id="LC509" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">When <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> every principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> admits an essentially unique (up to the action of the Weyl group) holomorphic reduction of structure group to a maximal torus <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GrothendieckSphere}.  Since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections for an abelian group are automatically stable, polystability on the sphere is equivalent to admissibility of the torus reduction.  As a consequence, for our main example of interest -- the rational case -- the moduli space of polystable <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections is equivalent to the moduli space of all <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections of admissible degree.  For instance for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G=<span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the moduli space of polystable <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection is equivalent to the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections on the trivial bundle.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L510" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="510"></td>
        <td id="LC510" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L511" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="511"></td>
        <td id="LC511" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Poisson Structures from Derived Geometry}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L512" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="512"></td>
        <td id="LC512" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As we mentioned above in Remark \ref{Elliptic_AKSZ_remark}, in the case where $C$ is an elliptic curve and there are no punctures there is a symplectic structure on $\mhiggs_G(C)$ given by the AKSZ formalism.  More generally, when we do have punctures, we expect the moduli space $\mhiggs_G(C,D)$ to have a Poisson structure with a clear origin story coming from the theory of derived Poisson geometry.  In this section we&#39;ll explain what this story looks like.  However, we emphasise that there are technical obstructions to making this story precise with current technology: this section should be viewed as motivation for the structures we&#39;ll discuss in the rest of the paper.  On the other hand, readers who aren&#39;t familiar with derived symplectic geometry can freely skip this section.  We refer the reader to \cite{CPTVV} for the theory of derived Poisson structures and to \cite{MelaniSafronov1, MelaniSafronov2, Spaide} for that of derived coisotropic structures.  We would like to thank Pavel Safronov for explaining many of the ideas discussed in this section to us.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L513" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="513"></td>
        <td id="LC513" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L514" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="514"></td>
        <td id="LC514" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here&#39;s the idea.  Recall that we can identify the moduli space of singular <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections on a curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as a fiber product: <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C, D) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(C) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)^2} <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(C) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> (P|_{C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D}, q^*P|_{C <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Consider the following commutative cube:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L515" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="515"></td>
        <td id="LC515" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L516" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="516"></td>
        <td id="LC516" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\xymatrix@C</span>-30pt@R-8pt{</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L517" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="517"></td>
        <td id="LC517" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp; <span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C, D) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[rr]^{f_1} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>&#39;[d][dd]^(.25){<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{res}} &amp; &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[dd]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L518" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="518"></td>
        <td id="LC518" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L519" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="519"></td>
        <td id="LC519" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{&lt;-}[ur]^{f_2} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[rr]^(.6){g_2} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[dd] &amp; &amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D)^2 <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{&lt;-}[ur]^{g_1} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[dd]^(.4)r</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L520" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="520"></td>
        <td id="LC520" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L521" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="521"></td>
        <td id="LC521" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp; <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)^k <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>&#39;[r][rr] &amp; &amp; BL^+G^{2k}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L522" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="522"></td>
        <td id="LC522" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L523" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="523"></td>
        <td id="LC523" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">BLG^k <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[rr]<span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{&lt;-}[ur] &amp; &amp; BLG^{2k}. <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{&lt;-}[ur]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L524" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="524"></td>
        <td id="LC524" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L525" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="525"></td>
        <td id="LC525" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here the top and bottom faces are homotopy Cartesian squares.  What does this setup buy us?  We&#39;ll first answer informally.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L526" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="526"></td>
        <td id="LC526" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L527" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="527"></td>
        <td id="LC527" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{claim}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L528" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="528"></td>
        <td id="LC528" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">First consider the bottom face of the cube.  The stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>BLG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 2-shifted symplectic because the Lie algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a non-degenerate invariant pairing: the residue pairing.  The Lie subalgebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L^+<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> forms part of a Manin triple <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(L<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>, L^+<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>, L^-+<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which means that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>BL^+G <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BLG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 2-shifted Lagrangian.  Therefore the bottom face of the cube defines a 2-shifted Lagrangian intersection, which means that the pullback <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted symplectic.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L529" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="529"></td>
        <td id="LC529" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L530" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="530"></td>
        <td id="LC530" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now consider the top face of the cube.  If either <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an elliptic curve, or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C=<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and we fix a framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, then the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BLG^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is also 2-shifted Lagrangian.  In particular <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted Poisson.  Finally, the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted coisotropic, or equivalently the canonical map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{BLG^k} BL^+G^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted Lagrangian.  That means that the top face of the cube defines a 1-shifted coisotropic intersection, which means that the pullback <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 0-shifted Poisson.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L531" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="531"></td>
        <td id="LC531" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
