        <td id="L532" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="532"></td>
        <td id="LC532" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The restriction map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted Lagrangian, which means that if we form the intersection with a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-tuple of Lagrangians in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> then we obtain a 0-shifted symplectic stack.  For example, if <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_i^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a point in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> corresponding to a dominant coweight with stabilizer <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B <span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>_i <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 1-shifted Lagrangian, so the moduli stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> obtained by taking the derived intersection is ind 0-shifted symplectic.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L533" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="533"></td>
        <td id="LC533" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{claim}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L534" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="534"></td>
        <td id="LC534" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L535" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="535"></td>
        <td id="LC535" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, let us make this claim more precise.  The main technical condition that makes this claim subtle comes from the fact that most of the derived stacks appearing in this cube, for instance the stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>BLG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, are not Artin.  As such we need to be careful when we try to, for instance, talk about the tangent complex to such stacks.  One can make careful statements using the formalism of ``Tate stacks&#39;&#39; developed by Hennion <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Hennion}.  We can therefore make our claim into a more formal conjecture.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L536" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="536"></td>
        <td id="LC536" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L537" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="537"></td>
        <td id="LC537" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L538" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="538"></td>
        <td id="LC538" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Suppose <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is either an elliptic curve or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a fixed framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L539" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="539"></td>
        <td id="LC539" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L540" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="540"></td>
        <td id="LC540" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>BLG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is Tate 2-shifted symplectic, and both <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>BL^+G <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BLG<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BLG^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are Tate 2-shifted Lagrangian.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L541" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="541"></td>
        <td id="LC541" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is ind 1-shifted Poisson, and the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is ind 1-shifted coisotropic witnessed by the 2-shifted Lagrangian map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>BL^+G^k <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> BLG^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L542" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="542"></td>
        <td id="LC542" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The Lagrangian intersection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is Tate 1-shifted symplectic, and the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>_i <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> associated to the inclusion of the stabilizer of a closed point is 1-shifted Lagrangian.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L543" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="543"></td>
        <td id="LC543" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L544" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="544"></td>
        <td id="LC544" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As a consequence, the moduli stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is ind 0-shifted Poisson and the moduli stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 0-shifted symplectic.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L545" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="545"></td>
        <td id="LC545" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L546" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="546"></td>
        <td id="LC546" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L547" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="547"></td>
        <td id="LC547" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L548" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="548"></td>
        <td id="LC548" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We should explain heuristically why the Calabi-Yau condition on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is necessary.  This is a consequence of the AKSZ formalism in the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is empty: for the mapping stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C, G/G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be 0-shifted symplectic, or for the mapping stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C,BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be 1-shifted symplectic, we need <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be compact and 1-oriented.  A <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-orientation on a smooth complex variety of dimension <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is exactly the same as a Calabi-Yau structure.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L549" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="549"></td>
        <td id="LC549" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L550" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="550"></td>
        <td id="LC550" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">More generally we can say the following.  Let us consider the rational case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Consider the inclusion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> r <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_- = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)}[-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> r^*<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{BLG^k}[-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] = <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: a map of ind-pro Lie algebras concentrated in degree zero.  The residue pairing vanishes after pulling back along <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> since elements of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_-<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued functions on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with at least a simple pole at every puncture in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  So the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is isotropic with zero isotropic structure; this structure is unique for degree reasons.  We must check that this structure is non-degenerate.  It suffices to check that the sequence</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L551" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="551"></td>
        <td id="LC551" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)}[-1] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> r^*<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{BLG^k}[-1] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> (<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)}[-1])^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L552" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="552"></td>
        <td id="LC552" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">is an exact sequence of ind-pro vector spaces, and therefore an exact sequence of quasi-coherent sheaves on the stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  To do this we identify the pair <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_-, <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)^k)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as part of a Manin triple, where a complementary isotropic subalgebra to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_-<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_+ = <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[[z]]^k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Using the residue pairing we can identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_+<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_-)^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and therefore identify our sequence with the split exact sequence</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L553" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="553"></td>
        <td id="LC553" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>0 <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_- <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)^k <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_+ <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> 0.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L554" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="554"></td>
        <td id="LC554" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L555" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="555"></td>
        <td id="LC555" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L556" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="556"></td>
        <td id="LC556" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L557" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="557"></td>
        <td id="LC557" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We will conclude this section with some comments on the multiplicative Hitchin system described above in Section \ref{Hitchin_system_section}.  In particular, the derived point of view suggests that both the multiplicative Hitchin fibers and the multiplicative Hitchin section of Remark \ref{q_opers_remark} will be -- at least generically -- canonically Lagrangian.  We can motivate this directly from the Chevalley map $\chi \colon G/G \to T/W$, by studying the non-singular example.  Generically, i.e. after restricting to the regular semisimple locus, we can identify $G^{\mr{rss}}/G$ with $(T^{\mr{reg}} \times BT)/W$, so that the fibers of the tangent space to $G/G$ are generically equivalent to $\mf t[1] \oplus \mf t$.  The directions tangent to the generic fibers of $\chi$ are concentrated in degree $-1$, meaning that the generic fibers of $\chi$ are canonically 1-shifted Lagrangian for degree reasons.  Likewise, the directions tangent to the Steinberg section $\sigma \colon T/W \to G/G$, at regular semisimple points, are concentrated in degree 0, meaning that after restriction to the regular semisimple locus is also canonically 1-shifted Lagrangian for degree reasons.  Now, if $L \to X$ is $n$-shifted Lagrangian and $M$ is $k$-oriented then there is an AKSZ $n-k$-shifted Lagrangian structure on the mapping space $\map(M,L) \to \map(M,X)$ \cite[Theorem 2.10]{Calaque}, which establishes our claim in the non-singular case. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L558" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="558"></td>
        <td id="LC558" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L559" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="559"></td>
        <td id="LC559" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We should compare this discussion to Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Hitchin_isotropic_prop} in the rational case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where we prove that, in the rational case, the generic multiplicative Hitchin fibers are, indeed, Lagrangian.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L560" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="560"></td>
        <td id="LC560" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L561" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="561"></td>
        <td id="LC561" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L562" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="562"></td>
        <td id="LC562" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Bouthier_remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L563" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="563"></td>
        <td id="LC563" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There&#39;s yet another perspective that one might hope to pursue in order to define our symplectic structures in the language of derived symplectic geometry.  Bouthier \cite{Bouthier2} gave a description of the multiplicative Hitchin system along the following lines.  The Vinberg semigroup $V_G$ of $G$ is a family of affine schemes over $\CC^r$ whose generic fiber is isomorphic to $G$ but whose fibers lying on coordinate hyperplanes correspond to various degenerations of $G$.  Bouthier showed that the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles is equivalent to the moduli space of $G$-bundles, along with a section of an associated bundle $V_G^{\omega^\vee}$ built from the Vinberg semigroup and the data of the coloured divisor $(D,\omega^\vee)$.  It&#39;s reasonable to ask whether one can construct an AKSZ shifted symplectic structure on the moduli space from this point of view, using the oriented structure on $(\bb{CP}^1,\infty)$ and the results of Ginzburg and Rozenblyum on shifted symplectic structures on spaces of sections \cite{GinzburgRozenblyum}.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L564" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="564"></td>
        <td id="LC564" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L565" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="565"></td>
        <td id="LC565" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L566" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="566"></td>
        <td id="LC566" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Twisted Gauge Theory} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{twist_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L567" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="567"></td>
        <td id="LC567" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Before we move on to the main mathematical content of the paper, we&#39;ll digress a little to talk about one situation where multiplicative Hitchin systems appear in gauge theory.  This story was our original motivation for studying the objects appearing in this paper, but we should emphasise that it is quite independent from the rest of the paper.  The reader who is only interested in algebraic and symplectic geometry, and not in gauge theory, can safely skip this section.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L568" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="568"></td>
        <td id="LC568" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L569" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="569"></td>
        <td id="LC569" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll describe our multiplicative Hitchin systems as the moduli spaces of solutions to the classical equations of motion in certain twisted five-dimensional supersymmetric gauge theories.  This story is distinct from the appearance of the moduli space in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun} as the Seiberg-Witten integral system of a 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> theory.  Instead the moduli space will appear as the moduli space of solutions to the equations of motion in a twisted 5d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> supersymmetric gauge theory, compactified on a circle.  This story will be directly analogous to the occurence of the ordinary moduli stack of Higgs bundles in a holomorphic twist of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> theory (see <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloSH,ElliottYoo1} for a discussion of this story); we&#39;ll recover that example in the limit where the radius of the circle shrinks to zero.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L570" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="570"></td>
        <td id="LC570" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L571" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="571"></td>
        <td id="LC571" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Background on Supersymmetry and Twisting}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L572" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="572"></td>
        <td id="LC572" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L573" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="573"></td>
        <td id="LC573" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We should begin by briefly recalling the idea behind twisting for supersymmetric field theories.  This idea goes back to Witten <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{WittenTQFT}.  Supersymmetric field theories have odd symmetries coming from odd elements of the supersymmetry algebra.  Choose such an odd element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the property that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[Q,Q]=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defines an odd endomorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nu</span>(Q)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the algebra of observables of the supersymmetric field theory with the property that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nu</span>(Q)^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> = <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{twisted algebra of observables} associated to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the cohomology of the operator <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nu</span>(Q)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is chosen appropriately -- if the stress-energy tensor of the theory is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nu</span>(Q)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-exact -- then the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted field theory becomes topological.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L574" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="574"></td>
        <td id="LC574" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L575" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="575"></td>
        <td id="LC575" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L576" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="576"></td>
        <td id="LC576" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From a modern perspective, using the language of factorization algebras, the first author and P. Safronov discussed the formalism behind topological twisting in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ElliottSafronov}, and gave criteria for twisted quantum field theories to genuinely be topological.  The supersymmetry algebras and their loci of square zero elements are discussed in all cases in dimensions up to 10.  This classification is also performed in a paper of Eager, Saberi and Walcher <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{EagerSaberiWalcher}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L577" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="577"></td>
        <td id="LC577" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L578" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="578"></td>
        <td id="LC578" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L579" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="579"></td>
        <td id="LC579" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">With the basic idea in hand, we&#39;ll focus in on the example we&#39;re interested in.  We&#39;ll be interested in twists by square-zero supercharges <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that are not fully topological.  We&#39;ll begin by describing the supercharges we&#39;ll be interested in in dimensions 5 and 6.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L580" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="580"></td>
        <td id="LC580" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L581" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="581"></td>
        <td id="LC581" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Recall that there is an exceptional isomorphism identifying the groups <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Spin</span>(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{USp}(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The Dirac spinor representation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Spin</span>(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is four dimensional: under the above exceptional isomorphism it is identified with the defining representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{USp}(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Likewise there is an exceptional isomorphism identifying the groups <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Spin</span>(<span class="pl-c1">6</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SU</span>(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The two Weyl spinor representations <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are four dimensional: under the exceptional isomorphism they are identified with the defining representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SU</span>(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and its dual.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L582" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="582"></td>
        <td id="LC582" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L583" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="583"></td>
        <td id="LC583" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L584" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="584"></td>
        <td id="LC584" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The complexified <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> supersymmetry algebra in dimension 5 is the super Lie algebra</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L585" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="585"></td>
        <td id="LC585" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^5_k = (<span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(4;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(2k;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)_R <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> V) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>(S <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> W),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L586" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="586"></td>
        <td id="LC586" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the five-dimensional defining representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\so</span>(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-dimensional defining representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>k;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and where there&#39;s a unique non-trivial way of defining an additional bracket <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gamma</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sym</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>(S <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> W) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L587" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="587"></td>
        <td id="LC587" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L588" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="588"></td>
        <td id="LC588" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Likewise, the complexified <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(k_+,k_-)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> supersymmetry algebra in dimension 6 is the super Lie algebra</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L589" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="589"></td>
        <td id="LC589" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^6_{(k_+,k_-)} = (<span class="pl-c1">\sl</span>(4;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(2k_+;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)_{R} <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(2k_-;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)_R <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> V) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Pi</span>(S_+ <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> W_+ <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> S_- <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> W_-),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L590" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="590"></td>
        <td id="LC590" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the six-dimensional defining representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\so</span>(<span class="pl-c1">6</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sl</span>(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span>k_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-dimensional defining representation of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>k_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and where there&#39;s a unique non-trivial way of defining an additional bracket <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gamma</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sym</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span>(S_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span> <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> W_<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Choosing a hyperplane in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defines a super Lie algebra map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">5</span>_{k_+ + k_-} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">6</span>_{(k_+,k_-)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which is an isomorphism on the odd summands.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L591" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="591"></td>
        <td id="LC591" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L592" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="592"></td>
        <td id="LC592" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L593" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="593"></td>
        <td id="LC593" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us fix some notation for the square-zero supercharges -- odd elements <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gamma</span>(Q,Q)=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- that we will refer to in the discussion below.  Fix once and for all an embedding <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">5</span> <span class="pl-c1">\inj</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">6</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a symplectic embedding <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W_+ <span class="pl-c1">\inj</span> W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (the twisted theories that we&#39;ll define don&#39;t depend on these choices).  Compare to the discussion in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[4.2.5--4.2.6]{ElliottSafronov}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L594" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="594"></td>
        <td id="LC594" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L595" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="595"></td>
        <td id="LC595" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}} <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">5</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be any non-zero element such that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gamma</span>(Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}},Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}})=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- here ``min&#39;&#39; stands for ``minimal&#39;&#39;.  All such elements have rank one, and lie in a single orbit for the action of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\so</span>(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The image <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gamma</span>(Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}}, -) <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 3-dimensional.  Using the given embeddings we can view <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> equally as an element of the larger supersymmetry algebras <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">5</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">6</span>_{(1,0)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">6</span>_{(1,1)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L596" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="596"></td>
        <td id="LC596" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{HT}} = Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}} + Q&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">5</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a non-zero element that squares to zero, and where the image <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Gamma</span>(Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}}, -) <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">5</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is 4-dimensional -- here ``HT&#39;&#39; stands for ``holomorphic-topological&#39;&#39;.  All such elements have rank two and lie in a single orbit under the action of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\so</span>(<span class="pl-c1">5</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sp</span>(<span class="pl-c1">4</span>;<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Using the given embedding <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">5</span> <span class="pl-c1">\inj</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">6</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we can view <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> equially as an element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> A^<span class="pl-c1">6</span>_{(1,1)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L597" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="597"></td>
        <td id="LC597" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L598" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="598"></td>
        <td id="LC598" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L599" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="599"></td>
        <td id="LC599" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Description of the Twist}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L600" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="600"></td>
        <td id="LC600" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Having set up our notation, we can state one the way in which the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles arises from twisted supersymmetric gauge theory.  We will first state the relationship, then explain what exactly the statement is supposed to mean.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L601" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="601"></td>
        <td id="LC601" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L602" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="602"></td>
        <td id="LC602" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{claimnum} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{twist_claim}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L603" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="603"></td>
        <td id="LC603" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If we take the twist of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory with gauge group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, on the 5-manifold <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a Calabi-Yau curve, with monopole surface operators placed at the points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>), <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, (z_k,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with charges <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_1}, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_k}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> respectively, its moduli space of solutions to the equations of motion can be identified with the shifted cotangent space</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L604" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="604"></td>
        <td id="LC604" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{EOM}_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^2) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> T^*[1]<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L605" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="605"></td>
        <td id="LC605" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{claimnum}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L606" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="606"></td>
        <td id="LC606" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L607" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="607"></td>
        <td id="LC607" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L608" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="608"></td>
        <td id="LC608" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The shifted cotangent space of a stack is a natural construction in the world of derived geometry.  In brief, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-shifted cotangent space of a stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a canonical projection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> T^*[k]<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the fiber over a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a derived affine space (i.e. a cochain complex) -- the tangent space to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> shifted down in cohomological degree by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L609" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="609"></td>
        <td id="LC609" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L610" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="610"></td>
        <td id="LC610" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L611" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="611"></td>
        <td id="LC611" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">So, let us try to unpack the meaning of Claim <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{twist_claim}.  Firstly, what does it mean to identify ``the moduli stack of solutions to the equations of motion&#39;&#39; of our twisted theory?  We have the following idea in mind (discussed in more detail, for instance, in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloSUSY, ElliottYoo1}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L612" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="612"></td>
        <td id="LC612" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L613" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="613"></td>
        <td id="LC613" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{construction} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{twist_construction}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L614" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="614"></td>
        <td id="LC614" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll use the Lagrangian description for the twisted field theory.  On the one hand, we can describe a twisted space of fields and twisted action functional.  This is a fairly standard construction: one factors the action functional into the sum <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{tw}}(<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>) + Q<span class="pl-c1">\Lambda</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of a ``twisted&#39;&#39; action functional and a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-exact functional.  Note that the action of the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Spin</span>(n) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> G_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the group of R-symmetries, is broken to a subgroup.  Only the subgroup of this product stabilizing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> still acts on the twisted theory. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L615" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="615"></td>
        <td id="LC615" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L616" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="616"></td>
        <td id="LC616" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Having written down the twisted action functional, we&#39;ll consider its critical locus: the moduli space of solutions to the equations of motion.  However, we can consider a finer invariant than only the ordinary critical locus: we can form the critical locus in the setting of derived geometry.  In classical field theory this idea is captured by the classical <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{BV formalism}: for a modern formulation see e.g. <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloBook}.  In particular, for each classical point in the critical locus, we can calculate the classical BV-BRST complex of the twisted theory -- concretely, we calculate the BV-BRST complex of the untwisted theory, and add the operator <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the differential.  The twisted BV-BRST complex models the tangent complex to the derived critical locus of the twisted theory.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L617" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="617"></td>
        <td id="LC617" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L618" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="618"></td>
        <td id="LC618" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">So, to summarize, the BV formalism gives us a space: the critical locus of the twisted action functional, equipped with a sheaf of cochain complexes, whose fiber at a solution is the twisted BV-BRST complex around that solution.  This structure is weaker than a derived stack, but when we say a derived stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> ``can be identified with&#39;&#39; the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\EOM</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of solutions to the equations of motion, we mean that we can identify the space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-points of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the analytic topology with the underlying space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\EOM</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and we can coherently identify the tangent complex of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the twisted BV-BRST complex at the corresponding classical solution.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L619" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="619"></td>
        <td id="LC619" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{construction}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L620" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="620"></td>
        <td id="LC620" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L621" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="621"></td>
        <td id="LC621" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L622" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="622"></td>
        <td id="LC622" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There&#39;s another subtlety that we glossed over in our discussion of the BV-BRST complex above: a priori when you add <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the differential of the untwisted BV-BRST complex the result is only <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span>/<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-graded, since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has ghost number 0 and superdegree 1, whereas the BV-BRST differential has ghost number 1 and superdegree 0.  In order to promote it to a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-graded complex we need to modify the degrees of our fields using an action of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span> U(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> inside the R-symmetry group, so that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has weight 1.  This is possible in all the examples we&#39;ll discuss below, and in our sketch argument we&#39;ll use this <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span> U(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> action to collapse the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span>/<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-grading down to a single <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-grading everywhere without further comment.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L623" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="623"></td>
        <td id="LC623" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L624" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="624"></td>
        <td id="LC624" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L625" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="625"></td>
        <td id="LC625" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now that we know what Claim <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{twist_claim} means, why is it true?  We&#39;ll only outline an argument here, since the whole twisted gauge theory story is somewhat orthogonal to the emphasis of the rest of this paper.  The outline we&#39;ll give goes via the minimal twist of 6d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory.  This calculation was done independently by Dylan Butson -- a detailed version will appear in his forthcoming article <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Butson}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L626" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="626"></td>
        <td id="LC626" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L627" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="627"></td>
        <td id="LC627" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L628" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="628"></td>
        <td id="LC628" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> First, compute the twist of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory in 6-dimensions by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{min}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This twisted theory is defined on a compact Calabi-Yau 3-fold <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X^<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and can be identified, in the sense of Construction <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{twist_construction}, with the shifted cotangent space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T^*[-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]<span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(X^<span class="pl-c1">3</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Note: there are at least two ways of doing this calculation.  One can calculate the twist directly using a method very similar to Baulieu&#39;s calculation of the minimal twist of 10-dimensional <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Baulieu}.  Alternatively one can work in a version of the first order formalism where one introduces an auxiliary 2-form field: this is the approach followed by Butson. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L629" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="629"></td>
        <td id="LC629" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L630" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="630"></td>
        <td id="LC630" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> One can extend this calculation to include a hypermultiplet valued in a representation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  One finds that the inclusion of the twisted hypermultiplet couples the moduli space of holomorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles to sections in the associated bundle corresponding to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  That is, the moduli space of solutions of the twisted theory can be identified with the shifted cotangent space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T^*[-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]<span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(X^<span class="pl-c1">3</span>, W/G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the quotient stack.  This tells us the twist of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills: this is the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W = <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

        <td id="LC632" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The twist by the holomorphic-topological supercharge <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{HT}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> corresponds to a deformation of this moduli space.       <tr>
        <td id="L638" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="638"></td>

        <td id="LC639" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> Now, all of these theories can be dimensionally reduced down to 5 dimensions.  Specifically, let us split <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> E_q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and send the radius of one of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> factors to zero, or equivalently degenerate the smooth elliptic curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E_q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to a nodal curve.  We&#39;re left with the identification, for the example we&#39;re interested in:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L640" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="640"></td>
        <td id="LC640" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\EOM</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> T^*[-1]<span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}, G/G).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L641" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="641"></td>
        <td id="LC641" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> Here we have identified <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(E^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{nod}}, BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the adjoint quotient <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> <span class="pl-c1">\footnote</span>{Strictly speaking this is only the semistable part of the moduli space.  We get <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, for instance, by asking for only those bundles which lift to the trivial bundle on the normalization.}.  So far, tn this discussion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> was a compact curve.  If we want to set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> instead the only change is that the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>-<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-shifted tangent space becomes the 1-shifted tangent complex.  There&#39;s a unique flat <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so we can identify</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L642" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="642"></td>
        <td id="LC642" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\EOM</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> T^*[1]<span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C, G/G).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L643" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="643"></td>
        <td id="LC643" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L644" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="644"></td>
        <td id="LC644" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\item</span> Finally, we need to include surface operators.  In order to see how to do this, let us go back to the Lagrangian description of our classical field theory.  The inclusion of monopole operators is usually thought of as modifying the space of fields in our supersymmetric gauge theory, so that the gauge field is permitted to be singular along the prescribed surface, with specified residues.  If we track the above calculation where the fields are allowed those prescribed singularities, the result is that we should replace <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> E^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{nod}}, BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the moduli space of singular multiplicative Higgs fields with local singularity data corresponding to the choice of charges of the monopole operators.  That is we can identify,</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L645" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="645"></td>
        <td id="LC645" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{EOM}_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^2) = T^*[1]<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
