      <tr>
        <td id="L648" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="648"></td>
        <td id="LC648" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}[Reduction to 4-dimensions]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L649" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="649"></td>
        <td id="LC649" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If we reduce further, to four dimensions, by sending the radius of the remaining <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to zero, then we recover a more familiar twist first defined by Kapustin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KapustinHolo}.  We can interpret this further degeneration as degenerating the factor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E_q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> not to a nodal, but to a cuspidal curve.  The semistable part of the stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(E^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{cusp}},BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on a cuspidal curve is equivalent the Lie algebra adjoint quotient stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so we can identify the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> theory with</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L650" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="650"></td>
        <td id="LC650" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L651" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="651"></td>
        <td id="LC651" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\EOM</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>) &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> T^*[-1]<span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}, <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>/G) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L652" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="652"></td>
        <td id="LC652" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> T^*[-1]<span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(T[1]C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}, BG).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L653" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="653"></td>
        <td id="LC653" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L654" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="654"></td>
        <td id="LC654" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is the shifted cotangent space whose base is the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a flat connection on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a Higgs field on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (note that this twisted theory is defined where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are any curves, not necessarily Calabi-Yau).  This agrees with the calculation performed in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ElliottYoo1}.  In particular, if we set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the result is</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L655" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="655"></td>
        <td id="LC655" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\EOM</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\HT</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> T^*[1]<span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G(C).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L656" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="656"></td>
        <td id="LC656" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L657" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="657"></td>
        <td id="LC657" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L658" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="658"></td>
        <td id="LC658" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Kapustin_twist_remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L659" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="659"></td>
        <td id="LC659" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This supersymmetric gauge theory story should be compared to several recent twisting calculations in the literature.  Firstly, the minimal twist of 5d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gauge theory was discussed by Qiu and Zabzine <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{QiuZabzine} on quite general contact five-manifolds.  They described the twisted equations of motion in terms of the Haydys-Witten equations.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L660" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="660"></td>
        <td id="LC660" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L661" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="661"></td>
        <td id="LC661" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A recent article of Costello and Yagi <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloYagi} also described a relationship between multiplicative Higgs moduli spaces and twisted supersymmetric gauge theory in yet another context.  They calculated the twist of 6d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gauge theory, but with respect to yet another twisting supercharge <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the property that the image of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[Q,-]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">6</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is five-dimensional.  They then consider this theory on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and place it in the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-background in the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> directions.  They argue that the resulting theory is a four-dimensional version Chern-Simons theory on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> holomorphic on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and topological in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L662" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="662"></td>
        <td id="LC662" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L663" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="663"></td>
        <td id="LC663" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-holomorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-topological 4d Chern-Simons theory on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  was introduced for the first time that we&#39;re aware of by Nekrasov in his Ph.D. thesis (page 89 of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovThesis}), where it was also conjectured that such a Chern-Simons theory</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L664" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="664"></td>
        <td id="LC664" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">would provide a new geometric origin for quantum affine algebras with spectral parameter on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The idea was recently revived by Costello <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloYangian}): the moduli stack of derived classical solutions of 4d Chern-Simons theory on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be identified with the mapping stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\map</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}, BG)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Nekrasov in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovStringMath} and Costello and Yagi in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloYagi}  go on to argue via a sequence of string dualities that this 4d CS theory is dual to the ADE quiver gauge theories discussed in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun, NekrasovPestunShatashvili}.  From another point of view, dualities of this form were also discussed by Ashwinkumar, Tan and Zhao <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{AshwinkumarTanZhao}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L665" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="665"></td>
        <td id="LC665" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L666" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="666"></td>
        <td id="LC666" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Heuristically speaking, the 4d Chern-Simons theory of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovThesis} and <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloYangian} on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{Dol}} <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{dR}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Sigma</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{dR}} = S^{1}_{dR} <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{R}_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{time}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> quantizes, in the path formalism, the holomorphic symplectic phase space of solutions to the Bogomolny monopole equations on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{Dol}} <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^{1}_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{dR}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, in the same way that ordinary 3d Cherns-Simons theory on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{dR}} <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{R}_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{time}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  quantized the moduli space</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L667" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="667"></td>
        <td id="LC667" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">of flat connections on the Riemann surface <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{dR}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the work of Witten <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{witten1989}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L668" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="668"></td>
        <td id="LC668" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">While Costello <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloYangian} considers Wilson operators,  we consider Dirac singularties of the monopoles or, equivalently, t&#39;Hooft operators.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L669" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="669"></td>
        <td id="LC669" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L670" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="670"></td>
        <td id="LC670" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L671" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="671"></td>
        <td id="LC671" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Langlands Duality} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Langlands_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L672" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="672"></td>
        <td id="LC672" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Our main motivation for describing the multiplicative Hitchin system in terms of a twist of 5d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory is to make the first steps towards a ``multiplicative&#39;&#39; version of the geometric Langlands conjecture.  The description in terms of supersymmetric gauge theory allows us to use the description of the geometric Langlands conjecture in terms of S-duality for topological twists of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory given by Kapustin and Witten <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KapustinWitten}.  Better yet, Witten described S-duality in terms of the 6d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> superconformal field theory compactified on a torus: one obtains dual theories by compactifying on the two circles in either of the two possible orders <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Witten6d}.  We can leverage this story in order to describe a conjectural duality for twisted 5d gauge theories. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L673" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="673"></td>
        <td id="LC673" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L674" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="674"></td>
        <td id="LC674" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The A- and B-twists of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills can both be defined by deforming an intermediate twist sometimes referred to as the Kapustin twist <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KapustinHolo} (see <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CostelloSUSY, ElliottYoo1} for more details).  The moduli stack of solutions to the equations of motion on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the Kapustin twist is the 1-shifted cotangent space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: the moduli stack of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Higgs bundles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The A- and B-twists modify this in two different ways.  In the B-twist <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is deformed by a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler rotation, and it becomes <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Flat</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: the moduli stack of flat <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In the A-twist the shifted cotangent bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T^*[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]<span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is deformed to the de Rham stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\higgs</span>_G(C)_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- the de Rham stack of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has the property that quasi-coherent sheaves on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are the same as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L675" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="675"></td>
        <td id="LC675" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L676" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="676"></td>
        <td id="LC676" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To summarize Kapustin and Witten&#39;s argument therefore, S-duality interchanges the A- and B-twists of 4d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills thory,  and provides an equivalence between their respective categories of boundary conditions on the curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  These categories of boundary conditions can be identified on the B-side as the category of coherent sheaves on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Flat</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and on the A-side as the category of D-modules on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or equivalently coherent sheaves on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C)_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{dR}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L677" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="677"></td>
        <td id="LC677" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L678" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="678"></td>
        <td id="LC678" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, we observe that this family of twists arises as the limit of a family of twisted of 5d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gauge theory compactified on a circle, where the radius of the circle shrinks to zero.  This motivates an analogous five-dimensional story, which we summarize with the following ``pseudo-conjecture&#39;&#39;, by which we mean a physical statement whose correct mathematical formulation remains to be determined.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L679" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="679"></td>
        <td id="LC679" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L680" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="680"></td>
        <td id="LC680" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{pseudoconj}[Multiplicative Geometric Langlands] <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{multLanglands}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L681" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="681"></td>
        <td id="LC681" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a Langlands self-dual group.  There is an equivalence of categories</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L682" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="682"></td>
        <td id="LC682" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{A-Branes}_{q^{-1}}(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{B-Branes}(<span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L683" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="683"></td>
        <td id="LC683" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the category on the right-hand side depends on the value <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L684" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="684"></td>
        <td id="LC684" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{pseudoconj}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L685" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="685"></td>
        <td id="LC685" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L686" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="686"></td>
        <td id="LC686" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">What does this mean, and are there situations in which we can make it precise?  We&#39;ll discuss a few examples where we can say something more concrete.  In each case, by ``B-branes&#39;&#39; we&#39;ll just mean the category <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of coherent sheaves.  By ``A-branes&#39;&#39; we&#39;ll mean some version of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference modules} on the stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L687" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="687"></td>
        <td id="LC687" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L688" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="688"></td>
        <td id="LC688" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L689" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="689"></td>
        <td id="LC689" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This equivalence is supposed to interchange objects corresponding to branes of opers on the two sides, and introduce an analogue of the Feigin-Frenkel isomorphism between deformed W-algebras (see <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FrenkelReshetikhinSTS, STSSevostyanov}.  This isomorphism only holds for self-dual groups, which motivates the restriction to the self-dual case here.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L690" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="690"></td>
        <td id="LC690" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L691" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="691"></td>
        <td id="LC691" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L692" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="692"></td>
        <td id="LC692" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L693" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="693"></td>
        <td id="LC693" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Even for the ordinary geometric Langlands conjecture there are additional complications that we aren&#39;t addressing here.  For example, the most natural categorical version of the geometric Langlands conjecture is false for all non-abelian groups.  Arinkin and Gaitsgory <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ArinkinGaitsgory} explained how to correct the statement to obtain a believable conjecture: one has to consider not all coherent sheaves on the B-side, but only those sheaves satisfying a ``singular support&#39;&#39; condition.  In <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ElliottYoo2} it was argued that, from the point of view of twisted <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">4</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> super Yang-Mills theory these singular support conditions arise when one restricts to only those boundary conditions compatible with a choice of vacuum.  The same sorts of subtleties should equally occur in the multiplicative setting.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L694" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="694"></td>
        <td id="LC694" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L695" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="695"></td>
        <td id="LC695" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L696" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="696"></td>
        <td id="LC696" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{The Abelian Case}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L697" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="697"></td>
        <td id="LC697" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Suppose <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (more generally we could consider a higher rank abelian gauge group).  In general for an abelian group the moduli spaces we have defined are trivial -- for instance the rational and trigonometric spaces are always discrete.  However there is one interesting non-trivial example: the elliptic case.  For simplicity let us consider the abelian situation with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D = <span class="pl-c1">\emptyset</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: the case with no punctures.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L698" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="698"></td>
        <td id="LC698" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L699" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="699"></td>
        <td id="LC699" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L700" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="700"></td>
        <td id="LC700" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference module} on a variety <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with automorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a module for the sheaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Delta</span>_{q,X}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of non-commutative rings generated by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>_X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and an invertible generator <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the relation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cdot</span> f = q^*(f) <span class="pl-c1">\cdot</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\diff</span>_q(X)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the category of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-difference modules on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L701" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="701"></td>
        <td id="LC701" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L702" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="702"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L703" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="703"></td>
        <td id="LC703" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the abelian case the space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>(1)}(E)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is actually a stack, but one can split off the stacky part to define difference modules on it.  Indeed, for any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> one can write</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L705" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="705"></td>
        <td id="LC705" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and so</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L706" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="706"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L707" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="707"></td>
        <td id="LC707" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">which means one can define difference modules on these stacks associated to an automorphism of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> respectively.</td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L710" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="710"></td>
        <td id="LC710" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is an equivalence of categories for any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>

        <td id="L717" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="717"></td>
        <td id="LC717" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is an equivalence of categories for any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, q_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>

      </tr>

        <td id="L720" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="720"></td>

        <td id="L721" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="721"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L722" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="722"></td>
        <td id="LC722" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This conjecture should be provable using the same techniques as the ordinary geometric Langlands correspondence in the abelian case, i.e. by a (quantum) twisted Fourier-Mukai transform (as constructed by Polishchuk and Rothstein <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{PolishchukRothstein}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L723" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="723"></td>
        <td id="LC723" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L724" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="724"></td>
        <td id="LC724" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsubsection</span>{The Classical Case}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L725" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="725"></td>
        <td id="LC725" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, let us consider the limit <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This will give a conjectural statement involving coherent sheaves on both sides analogous to the classical limit of the geometric Langlands conjecture as conjectured by Donagi and Pantev <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{DonagiPantev}.  The existence of an equivalence isn&#39;t so interesting in the self-dual case (where both sides are the same), but the classical multiplicative Langlands functor should be an <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{interesting} non-trivial equivalence.  For example we can make the following conjecture</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L726" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="726"></td>
        <td id="LC726" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L727" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="727"></td>
        <td id="LC727" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L728" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="728"></td>
        <td id="LC728" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a Langlands self-dual group and let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be an elliptic curve.  There is an automorphism of categories (for the rational, trigonometric and elliptic moduli spaces)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L729" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="729"></td>
        <td id="LC729" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>F <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(E)) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_{G}(E))<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L730" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="730"></td>
        <td id="LC730" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">so that the following square commutes:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L731" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="731"></td>
        <td id="LC731" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\xymatrix</span>{</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L732" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="732"></td>
        <td id="LC732" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_T(E)) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r]^{<span class="pl-c1">\mathrm</span>{FM}} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d]_{p_*q^!} &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_T(E)) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d]^{p_*q^!} <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L733" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="733"></td>
        <td id="LC733" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(E)) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r]^{F} &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(E)).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L734" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="734"></td>
        <td id="LC734" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L735" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="735"></td>
        <td id="LC735" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here we&#39;re using the natural morphisms <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_B(E) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(E)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_B(E) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_T(E)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{FM}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the Fourier-Mukai transform.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L736" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="736"></td>
        <td id="LC736" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L737" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="737"></td>
        <td id="LC737" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L738" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="738"></td>
        <td id="LC738" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Alternatively, we can say something about classical geometric Langlands duality in the non-simply-laced case.  Recall in the usual geometric Langlands story that non-simply-laced gauge theories in dimension 4 arise by ``folding&#39;&#39; the Dynkin diagram.  In other words, one identifies a non-simply laced simple Lie group as the invariants of a simply laced self-dual Lie group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with respect to its finite group of outer automorphisms (either <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span>/<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the case of the exceptional group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).  One obtains a 5d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> gauge theory with gauge group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by taking the invariants of the 6d <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> N=(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> theory reduced on a circle, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Out}(<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> acts simultaneously on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and on the circle we reduce along.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L739" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="739"></td>
        <td id="LC739" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L740" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="740"></td>
        <td id="LC740" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Putting this together yields the following conjecture.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L741" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="741"></td>
        <td id="LC741" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L742" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="742"></td>
        <td id="LC742" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{eq:classical-q-langlands}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L743" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="743"></td>
        <td id="LC743" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be Langlands dual simple Lie groups, and say that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> arose by folding the Dynkin diagram of a self-dual group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Then there is an equivalence of categories</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L744" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="744"></td>
        <td id="LC744" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_{G^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}(E) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\coh</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G}(E)^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Out}(<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G)}),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L745" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="745"></td>
        <td id="LC745" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Out}(<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> acts simultaneously on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and on the circle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, under the identification <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G}(E) = <span class="pl-c1">\bun</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> G}(E <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  As above, this equivalence should be compatible with the Fourier-Mukai transform relating the categories for the maximal tori.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L746" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="746"></td>
        <td id="LC746" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L747" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="747"></td>
        <td id="LC747" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L748" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="748"></td>
        <td id="LC748" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L749" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="749"></td>
        <td id="LC749" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Periodic Monopoles} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{periodic_monopole_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L750" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="750"></td>
        <td id="LC750" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Moduli spaces of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections on a Riemann surface <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are closely related to moduli spaces of periodic monopoles, i.e. monopoles on 3-manifolds that fiber over the circle (more specifically, with fiber <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and monodromy determined by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a compact Lie group whose complexification is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The discussion in this section will mostly follow that of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CharbonneauHurtubise, Smith}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L751" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="751"></td>
        <td id="LC751" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L752" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="752"></td>
        <td id="LC752" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M = C<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with monodromy given by the automorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More precisely, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the Riemannian 3-manifold obtained by gluing the ends of the product <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> [<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of Riemannian manifolds by the isometry <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(x,<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R) <span class="pl-c1">\sim</span> (q(x), <span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L753" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="753"></td>
        <td id="LC753" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L754" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="754"></td>
        <td id="LC754" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L755" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="755"></td>
        <td id="LC755" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">A <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{monopole} on the Riemannian 3-manifold <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M = C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a smooth principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> equipped with a connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the associated bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> satisfying the Bogomolny equation </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L756" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="756"></td>
        <td id="LC756" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\ast</span> F_A = <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_A <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L757" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="757"></td>
        <td id="LC757" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L758" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="758"></td>
        <td id="LC758" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L759" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="759"></td>
        <td id="LC759" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L760" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="760"></td>
        <td id="LC760" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We should emphasise the difference between the Riemannian 3-manifold <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M = C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> appearing in this section and the derived stack <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (the mapping torus) appearing in the previous section.  These should be thought of as smooth and algebraic realizations of the same object (justified by the comparison Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{monopole_qconn_comparison_thm}) but they are a priori defined in different mathematical contexts.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L761" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="761"></td>
        <td id="LC761" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L762" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="762"></td>
        <td id="LC762" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L763" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="763"></td>
        <td id="LC763" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can rephrase the data of a monopole on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as follows.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the fiber over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, viewed as a Riemann surface.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the restriction of the complexified bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P_<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Consider first the restriction of the complexification of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to a connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> part of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> automatically defines a holomorphic structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can introduce an additional piece of structure on this holomorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle.  In order to do so we can decompose the Bogomolny equation into one real and one complex equation as follows.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L764" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="764"></td>
        <td id="LC764" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L765" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="765"></td>
        <td id="LC765" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">F_{A_0} - <span class="pl-c1">\nabla</span>_t <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span> &amp;= 0 <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L766" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="766"></td>
        <td id="LC766" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">[<span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\del</span>}_{A_0}, <span class="pl-c1">\nabla</span>_t - i<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t] &amp;= 0 </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L767" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="767"></td>
        <td id="LC767" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L768" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="768"></td>
        <td id="LC768" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nabla</span>_t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the component of the covariant derivative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> normal to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L769" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="769"></td>
        <td id="LC769" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L770" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="770"></td>
        <td id="LC770" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition} </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L771" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="771"></td>
        <td id="LC771" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From now on we&#39;ll use the notation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the combination <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nabla</span>_t - i<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: an element of the space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P)<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of sections of the complex vector bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on the complex curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L772" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="772"></td>
        <td id="LC772" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L773" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="773"></td>
        <td id="LC773" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L774" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="774"></td>
        <td id="LC774" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us now introduce singularities into the story.  We&#39;ll keep the description brief, referring the reader to <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CharbonneauHurtubise, Smith} for details.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L775" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="775"></td>
        <td id="LC775" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L776" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="776"></td>
        <td id="LC776" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a finite subset.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a choice of coweight for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  A monopole on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Dirac singularity} at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with charge <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if locally on a neighborhood of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> it is obtained by pulling back under <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the standard Dirac monopole solution to the Bogomolny equation, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is spherically symmetric with a simple pole at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the restriction of a connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to a two-sphere <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> enclosing the singularity defines a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> bundle on this <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of degree <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> so that</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L777" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="777"></td>
        <td id="LC777" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{1}{2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{S^2} F = 1 .<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L778" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="778"></td>
        <td id="LC778" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  See e.g. <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 2.2]{CharbonneauHurtubise} for a more detailed description.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L779" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="779"></td>
        <td id="LC779" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L780" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="780"></td>
        <td id="LC780" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L781" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="781"></td>
        <td id="LC781" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can also introduce a framing (or a reduction of structure group as in the trigonometric example, though we won&#39;t consider the latter in this paper).  As usual let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a point fixed by the automorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L782" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="782"></td>
        <td id="LC782" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L783" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="783"></td>
        <td id="LC783" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  A monopole on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{framing} at the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a monopole <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P,A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (possibly with Dirac singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) along with a trivialization of the restriction of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the circle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, with the condition that the holonomy of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> around this circle lies in a fixed conjugacy class <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L784" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="784"></td>
        <td id="LC784" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L785" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="785"></td>
        <td id="LC785" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L786" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="786"></td>
        <td id="LC786" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The moduli theory of monopoles on general compact 3-manifolds was described by Pauly <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Pauly}.  In this paper we&#39;ll be interested in moduli spaces of monopoles on 3-manifolds of the form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, possibly with a fixed framing at a point in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L787" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="787"></td>
        <td id="LC787" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L788" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="788"></td>
        <td id="LC788" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L789" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="789"></td>
        <td id="LC789" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The moduli space of periodic monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> specifically has been studied in the mathematics literature by Foscolo <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FoscoloDef} , applying the analytic techniques of deformation theory to earlier work on periodic monopoles by Cherkis and Kapustin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CherkisKapustin1, CherkisKapustin2}. This analysis considers a less restrictive boundary condition at infinity in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> than a framing, and therefore requires more sophisticated analysis than we&#39;ll need to consider in the present paper.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L790" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="790"></td>
        <td id="LC790" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L791" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="791"></td>
        <td id="LC791" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L792" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="792"></td>
        <td id="LC792" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the cases of interest to us the moduli space of periodic monopoles can be obtained as a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler quotient.  Let us focus initially on the rational case, meaning monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with Dirac singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Consider the infinite-dimensional vector space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consisting of pairs <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a connection on a fixed principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a section of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> have a Dirac singularity with charge <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z_i,t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the group of gauge transformations of the bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L793" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="793"></td>

        <td id="L794" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="794"></td>
        <td id="LC794" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler moment map is given by the Bogomolny functional, namely</td>
      </tr>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L801" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="801"></td>
        <td id="LC801" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a finite subset <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span>(z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,t_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>), <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, (z_k, t_k)<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of points in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a choice of coweight for each point in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. The moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G(M, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler quotient</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L802" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="802"></td>
        <td id="LC802" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G(M, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\mu</span>^{-1}(0) / <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L803" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="803"></td>
        <td id="LC803" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
