        <td id="L804" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="804"></td>
        <td id="LC804" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L805" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="805"></td>
        <td id="LC805" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now let us address the relationship between periodic monopoles and</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L806" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="806"></td>
        <td id="LC806" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections.  Suppose from now on that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in the identity</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L807" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="807"></td>
        <td id="LC807" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">component of the group of automorphisms of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (fixing the framing</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L808" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="808"></td>
        <td id="LC808" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if present).  The following theorem is a slightly</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L809" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="809"></td>
        <td id="LC809" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">generalized version of the comparison theorem between multiplicative</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L810" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="810"></td>
        <td id="LC810" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Higgs bundles and periodic monopoles proved by Charbonneau--Hurtubise</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L811" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="811"></td>
        <td id="LC811" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CharbonneauHurtubise} for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and Smith <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Smith} for</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L812" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="812"></td>
        <td id="LC812" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">general <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. This approach was first suggested by Kapustin-Cherkis</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L813" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="813"></td>
        <td id="LC813" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CherkisKapustin2} under the name `spectral data&#39;. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L814" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="814"></td>
        <td id="LC814" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L815" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="815"></td>
        <td id="LC815" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{monopole_qconn_comparison_thm}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L816" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="816"></td>
        <td id="LC816" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is an analytic isomorphism between the moduli space of polystable monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with Dirac singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (and a possible framing on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) and the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More precisely there is an analytic isomorphism</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L817" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="817"></td>
        <td id="LC817" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>H <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>^{(<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>)}_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^1, D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>t_0<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,(fr)}}(C, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L818" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="818"></td>
        <td id="LC818" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">given by the holonomy map around <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. sending a monopole <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the holomorphic bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P = (<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P_<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)|_{C_0}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g = <span class="pl-c1">\Hol</span>_{S^1}(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> P <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> q^*(P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L819" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="819"></td>
        <td id="LC819" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L820" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="820"></td>
        <td id="LC820" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L821" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="821"></td>
        <td id="LC821" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L822" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="822"></td>
        <td id="LC822" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Note that in this statement we assumed that all the singularities occur in the same location in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. in the same slice <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> {t_0}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This assumption is not necessary, but there is a constraint on the possible locations of the singularities as explained in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Proposition 3.5]{CharbonneauHurtubise}.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L823" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="823"></td>
        <td id="LC823" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L824" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="824"></td>
        <td id="LC824" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L825" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="825"></td>
        <td id="LC825" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L826" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="826"></td>
        <td id="LC826" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This follows by the same argument as that given by Charbonneau--Hurtubise and Smith.  More explicitly, first let us think about injectivity, so let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P&#39;, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A&#39;)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a pair of periodic monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with images <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P&#39;, g&#39;)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> respectively, and choose a bundle isomorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\tau</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> P <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> P&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> intertwining the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  One observes first that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are also isomorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundles since, by intertwining with the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections, we have an isomorphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P|_{C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>t<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P&#39;|_{C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>t<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for every <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  That the monopole structures also match up follows by the same argument as in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Proposition 4.7]{CharbonneauHurtubise}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L827" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="827"></td>
        <td id="LC827" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L828" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="828"></td>
        <td id="LC828" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For surjectivity, again we&#39;ll match the argument in the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q=<span class="pl-c1">\id</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We begin by extending a holomorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>) = (C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R) <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> [-<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R,<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\aut</span>(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a geodesic with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(-<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R) = q^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)=<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R) = q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the 3-manifold</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L829" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="829"></td>
        <td id="LC829" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> M = ((-2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R, 2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> C) <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bigcup</span>_{j=1}^k (A^+_j <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> A^-_j)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L830" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="830"></td>
        <td id="LC830" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^+_j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the arc <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span>(t+ t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(t)(z_j)) <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> t <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R - t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>]<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A^-_j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the arc <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span>(t + t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> - <span class="pl-c1">4</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R,<span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(t)(z_j)) <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> t <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> [<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R-t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R)<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L831" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="831"></td>
        <td id="LC831" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L832" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="832"></td>
        <td id="LC832" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> M <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the projection sending <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(t,z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gamma</span>(t)(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> pulls back to a bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>^*(P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\wt</span> M<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We obtain a bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by applying the identification <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(t,z) <span class="pl-c1">\sim</span> (t - <span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R, q(z))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This bundle extends to an <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-invariant holomorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The remainder of the proof -- verifying the existence of the monopole structure associated to an appropriate choice of hermitian structure -- consists of local analysis which is independent of the value of the parameter <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L833" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="833"></td>
        <td id="LC833" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L834" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="834"></td>
        <td id="LC834" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It remains to remark on the compatibility of framing data on the two sides.  A trivialization of the bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> along the circle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> yields a trivialization of the fiber of the bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The condition that the holonomy around the circle at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fixes the value of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be in the conjugacy class <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L835" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="835"></td>

        <td id="L837" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="837"></td>
        <td id="LC837" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L838" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="838"></td>
        <td id="LC838" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Mochizuki <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Mochizuki} proved a stronger result in the rational case for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  He allows not just a framing at infinity in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> but also a singularity encoded in terms of a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-reduction of the bundle.  Again, we won&#39;t work in this generality in the present paper.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L839" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="839"></td>
        <td id="LC839" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L840" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="840"></td>
        <td id="LC840" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L841" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="841"></td>
        <td id="LC841" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Deformation Theory} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{def_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L842" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="842"></td>
        <td id="LC842" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the next section we&#39;ll compare symplectic forms on these moduli spaces.  In order to do so it will be important to understand the tangent spaces at a point of the source and target.  There&#39;s a natural description of these tangent spaces in terms of the hypercohomology of certain cochain complexes.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L843" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="843"></td>
        <td id="LC843" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L844" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="844"></td>
        <td id="LC844" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From now on we&#39;ll focus on the example we&#39;re most interested in.  That is, we&#39;ll exclusively study the rational situation where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and we fix a framing point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c = <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In this case we can use the description as a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler reduction.  For more general deformation theory calculations we refer to Foscolo <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FoscoloDef} (though the results in that paper are more broadly applicable).  Recall that we can write</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L845" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="845"></td>
        <td id="LC845" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>^{(<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>)}_G(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_q S^1, D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>t_0<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mu</span>^{-1}(0)/ <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L846" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="846"></td>
        <td id="LC846" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the group of gauge transformations of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mu</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> V <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(M; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_R)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the Bogomolny functional <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ast</span> F_A - <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_A <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The tangent complex to this hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler quotient at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be written as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(M <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P})[<span class="pl-c1">1</span>] <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\mu</span>^{-1}(0)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\mu</span>^{-1}(0)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the tangent complex to the zero locus of the moment map, concentrated in non-negative degrees. Roughly speaking <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\mu</span>^{-1}(0)} = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> T_{<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> V} <span class="pl-c1">\overset</span> {<span class="pl-c1">\d\mu</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(M; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_R)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P})[-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L847" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="847"></td>
        <td id="LC847" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L848" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="848"></td>
        <td id="LC848" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">More explicitly, following <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FoscoloDef} define <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be the sheaf of cochain complexes</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L849" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="849"></td>
        <td id="LC849" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\left</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\xymatrix</span>{</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L850" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="850"></td>
        <td id="LC850" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^0(M <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P}) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r]^(.36){<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_1} &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^1(M <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P}) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^0(M <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P}) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r]^(.64){<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_2} &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^1(M <span class="pl-cce">\!</span><span class="pl-c1">\bs</span><span class="pl-cce">\!</span> D; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P})</td>

        <td id="L855" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="855"></td>
        <td id="LC855" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Here we have chosen a point in the twistor sphere, forgetting the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure and retaining a holomorphic symplectic structure.  In other words we have identified the target of the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler moment map -- the space of imaginary quaternions -- with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span> <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which is equivalent to choosing a point in the unit sphere of the imaginary quaternions: the twistor sphere.  </td>

        <td id="LC869" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If one introduces a framing at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> then we must correspondingly twist the complex <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> above by the line bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(c)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- i.e. we restrict to sections that vanish at the framing point.         <td id="L875" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="875"></td>
        <td id="LC875" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L876" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="876"></td>
        <td id="LC876" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The tangent space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G(S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> C, D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P,<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is quasi-isomorphic to the hypercohomology <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(C <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>; <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F&#39;_{(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P,<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of a subsheaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where growth conditions are imposed on the degree 0 part of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> near the singularities.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L877" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="877"></td>
        <td id="LC877" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L878" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="878"></td>
        <td id="LC878" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L879" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="879"></td>
        <td id="LC879" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now let us consider the tangent complex to the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections.  For the arguments in this article we&#39;ll only need to carefully consider the case <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q=<span class="pl-c1">\id</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of multiplicative Higgs bundles, but we&#39;ll include some remarks regarding the more general case.  In this case the calculation was performed by Bottacin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Bottacin}, see also <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 4]{HurtubiseMarkman}. Fix a multiplicative Higgs bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We consider the sheaf of cochain complexes on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L880" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="880"></td>
        <td id="LC880" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F_{(P,g)} = (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P[1] <span class="pl-c1">\overset</span> {<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g} {<span class="pl-c1">\to</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P(-D))<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L881" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="881"></td>
        <td id="LC881" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in degrees <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>-<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and 0 with differential given by the adjoint action of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More precisely let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the bundle maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> obtained as the derivative of left- and right-multiplication.  Then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g = L_g - R_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can alternatively phrase this, as in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 4]{HurtubiseMarkman}, as follows.  Define <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be the vector bundle</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L882" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="882"></td>
        <td id="LC882" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g) = (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P)/<span class="pl-cce">\{</span>(X, -g X g^{-1}): X <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L883" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="883"></td>
        <td id="LC883" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Then we can write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as the sheaf of complexes</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L884" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="884"></td>
        <td id="LC884" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F_{(P,g)} = (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P[1] <span class="pl-c1">\overset</span> {<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g} {<span class="pl-c1">\to</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g))<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L885" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="885"></td>
        <td id="LC885" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where now <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is just the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> [(X,-X)]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L886" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="886"></td>
        <td id="LC886" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L887" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="887"></td>
        <td id="LC887" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L888" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="888"></td>
        <td id="LC888" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  If one introduces a framing at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> then we must correspondingly twist the complex <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> above by the line bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-c)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. we restrict to deformations that preserve the framing and therefore are zero at the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  So in that case we define</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L889" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="889"></td>
        <td id="LC889" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_{(P,g)} = (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P[1] <span class="pl-c1">\overset</span> {<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g} {<span class="pl-c1">\to</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P(-D)) <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-c).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L890" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="890"></td>

        <td id="L893" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="893"></td>
        <td id="LC893" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For more general <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we should modify this description by replacing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection.  Note that one can still define the (<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted) adjoint action <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> g X g^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> using a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connection, and so we can still define the complex</td>

        <td id="L894" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="894"></td>

        <td id="LC900" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{prop}[{<span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Proposition 3.1.3]{Bottacin}}]</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L901" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="901"></td>
        <td id="LC901" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The tangent space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(P,g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is quasi-isomorphic to the hypercohomology <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>(C; <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F_{(P,g)})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the sheaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L904" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="904"></td>
        <td id="LC904" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L905" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="905"></td>
        <td id="LC905" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The remaining hypercohomology of the sheaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F_{(P,g)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> generically has dimension <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\dim</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> z_{<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (or 0 if we fix a framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) in degree <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>-<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and dimension <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{genus}(C) <span class="pl-c1">\cdot</span> <span class="pl-c1">\dim</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> z_{<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in degree <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  However the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C, D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in fact a smooth algebraic variety.  This follows from a result of Hurtubise and Markman <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Theorem 4.13]{HurtubiseMarkman}, noting that their argument does not rely on the curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> being of genus 1.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L906" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="906"></td>

        <td id="L908" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="908"></td>
        <td id="LC908" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{corollary} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{dim_of_moduli_space_cor}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L909" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="909"></td>
        <td id="LC909" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the rational case, the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has dimension </td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L910" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="910"></td>
        <td id="LC910" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>2 <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{z_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D} <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i} <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L911" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="911"></td>
        <td id="LC911" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{corollary}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L912" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="912"></td>
        <td id="LC912" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L913" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="913"></td>
        <td id="LC913" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L914" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="914"></td>
        <td id="LC914" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One can use the same argument as <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{HurtubiseMarkman} (see also <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Proposition 5.6]{CharbonneauHurtubise}), with the additional observation that tensoring by the line bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> kills the outer cohomology groups (<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with our degree conventions, which differ from the conventions of loc. cit. by one).  Indeed, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consists of sections of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that are annihilated by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (given for generic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by constant sections valued in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> z_{<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) while vanish at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which are necessarily 0.  Likewise we can use the equivalence between the sheaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F_{(P,g)}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and its Serre dual to see that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> also vanishes.  Finally the Euler characteristic of the two step complex is unchanged by tensoring by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L915" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="915"></td>
        <td id="LC915" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L916" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="916"></td>
        <td id="LC916" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L917" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="917"></td>
        <td id="LC917" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to calculate with this hypercohomology group we&#39;ll use a <span class="pl-c1">\v</span> Cech resolution.  This will be straightforward for the multiplicative Higgs moduli space, and we&#39;ll use the isomorphism of Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{monopole_qconn_comparison_thm} to give an analogous description on the monopole side.    We define a cover <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> U = <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, U_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, U_k, U_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as follows.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a contractible open neighborhood of the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a contractible analytic open neighborhood of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> C<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, all chosen to be pairwise disjoint.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Finally let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Since the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are contractible and the remaining subset <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>c<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an affine algebraic curve, which means that for any quasi-coherent sheaf of cochain complexes the higher cohomology groups vanish.  Likewise for the intersections: the punctured open sets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are analytic open sets of an affine curve.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L918" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="918"></td>
        <td id="LC918" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L919" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="919"></td>
        <td id="LC919" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Specify a representative 0-cocycle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the <span class="pl-c1">\v</span> Cech cohomology group with respect to our chosen cover <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Explicitly a 0-cochain is given by the following data:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L920" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="920"></td>
        <td id="LC920" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>

        <td id="LC921" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g)(-1)(U_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>

        <td id="L923" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="923"></td>
        <td id="LC923" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_0 &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g)(C <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> (D <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>

        <td id="LC924" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P(U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L925" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="925"></td>
        <td id="LC925" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P(U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i) <span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ for } i=1,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L926" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="926"></td>
        <td id="LC926" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L927" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="927"></td>
        <td id="LC927" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the notation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> indicates tensoring by the line bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\pm</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L928" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="928"></td>
        <td id="LC928" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L929" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="929"></td>
        <td id="LC929" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Being a 0-cocycle means that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>} = <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_g(<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i} = <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_g(<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We consider 0-cocycles modulo 0-coboundaries of the form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_g(f_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>), <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_g(f_i)<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_g(f_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>), (f_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> -  f_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)|_{U_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>}, <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>(f_i - f_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)|_{U_i^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>}<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In fact <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Ad}_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an isomorphism on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the sections <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that occur: those with no poles or zeroes in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  That means that we can add a coboundary to force <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L930" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="930"></td>

</td>

        <td id="LC931" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, rather than describing the tangent space to the moduli space of monopoles we&#39;ll define a complex that maps to it which we can define locally with respect to the cover <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.         <td id="LC951" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To conclude this subsection it will also be important to have an explicit description of the derivative of the holonomy map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as a map between tangent spaces.  We can describe this map using our <span class="pl-c1">\v</span> Cech resolutions on each contractible open set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> individually.</td>

        <td id="L954" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="954"></td>
        <td id="LC954" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The derivative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^<span class="pl-c1">\bullet</span>(U_i <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> ; <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F&#39;_{(<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P,<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)}) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> H^<span class="pl-c1">\bullet</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D_i; <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F_{(P,g)})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is given on an open patch <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by the formula</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L955" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="955"></td>

      </tr>

        <td id="LC956" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i = <span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.       <tr>
        <td id="L960" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="960"></td>
        <td id="LC960" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Note that the right-hand side is the derivative at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_i <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> B_i(<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>)H(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)B_i(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">0</span>((U_i <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>)) <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span>(z_i, t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>; <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This is the definition of the action of the group of gauge transformations on the holonomy <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L961" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="961"></td>
        <td id="LC961" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L962" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="962"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L963" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="963"></td>
        <td id="LC963" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Symplectic Structures} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{symp_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L964" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="964"></td>
        <td id="LC964" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{An Example with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G=<span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{GL2_example_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L965" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="965"></td>
        <td id="LC965" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L966" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="966"></td>
        <td id="LC966" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us discuss in detail the geometry of the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles in some of the simplest examples, for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and minimal singularity data.  The symplectic structures, and the Hitchin integrable system, which we&#39;ll analyze for the more general moduli spaces can be described very concretely in this simple situation. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L967" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="967"></td>
        <td id="LC967" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L968" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="968"></td>
        <td id="LC968" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Fix <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G=<span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We&#39;ll work in the rational case, so we&#39;ll work over the curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cup</span> <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has coordinate <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, with fixed framing point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and fixed value <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the framing. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L969" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="969"></td>
        <td id="LC969" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L970" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="970"></td>
        <td id="LC970" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Consider the connected component of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_{G}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consisting of those multiplicative Higgs bundles whose underlying <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle is trivializable.  Fixing the framing fixes a trivialization of the underlying <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle, which means this connected component of the moduli space can be identified with the space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L971" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="971"></td>
        <td id="LC971" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">rational functions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with certain singularity conditions that we can write down explicitly.</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L973" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="973"></td>
        <td id="LC973" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">As our first explicit example we will consider the moduli space with two singularities at distinct points <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Fix the corresponding coweights to be the generators <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_1} = (<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_2} = (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the defining basis of the coweight lattice of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We&#39;ll denote the zero connected component in the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> M(z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,z_<span class="pl-c1">2</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1062" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1062"></td>
        <td id="LC1062" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can likewise calculate the multiplicative Hitchin section as in Remark <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{q_opers_remark} in this example.  The Steinberg section for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> sends a pair of eigenvalues <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(s,t) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the element</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1063" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1063"></td>
        <td id="LC1063" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{pmatrix}-s-t &amp; st <span class="pl-c1">\\</span> 1 &amp; 0<span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{pmatrix} <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1064" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1064"></td>
        <td id="LC1064" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to describe the multiplicative Hitchin section, let us use a framing that lands in the Steinberg section, say <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(a_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, b_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>,c_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, d_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>) = (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,-<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Then the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> M(z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,z_<span class="pl-c1">2</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as above with this framing can be identified with the smooth affine quadric surface </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1065" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1065"></td>
        <td id="LC1065" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{equation*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1066" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1066"></td>
        <td id="LC1066" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">        a_0d_0 + b_0^2  = m^2 .</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1067" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1067"></td>
        <td id="LC1067" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">    <span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{equation*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1068" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1068"></td>
        <td id="LC1068" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The multiplicative Hitchin section lies within the locus where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, i.e. to the pair of lines <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\pm</span> m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> inside our quadric surface.  The fixed framing at infinity picks out the line <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = - m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or the locus of matrices of the form </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1069" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1069"></td>
        <td id="LC1069" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>g(z) = <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{pmatrix} <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{a_0}{z-m} &amp; - <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{z+m}{z-m} <span class="pl-c1">\\</span> 1 &amp; 0<span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{pmatrix}.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1070" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1070"></td>
        <td id="LC1070" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In Poisson coordinates <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a,b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as above, the multiplicative Hitchin section is equivalent to the Lagrangian line <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>a = m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: a section of the projection map onto the space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on which <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a coordinate.    </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1071" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1071"></td>
        <td id="LC1071" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1072" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1072"></td>
        <td id="LC1072" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For a more general singularity datum, but for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G=<span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the multiplicative Hitchin section admits a similar description, where now the datum <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is encoded by a rational function <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(z)/p_<span class="pl-c1">2</span>(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p_<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are monic polynomials of the same degree, say <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The multiplicative Hitchin section then can be described as the locus of all matrices of the form</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1073" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1073"></td>
        <td id="LC1073" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>g(z) = <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{pmatrix} <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{q(z)}{p_2(z)} &amp; - <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{p_1(z)}{p_2(z)} <span class="pl-c1">\\</span> 1 &amp; 0<span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{pmatrix},<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1074" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1074"></td>
        <td id="LC1074" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a polynomial of degree less than <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (so the section is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-dimensional).  The sections which are in fact <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued are those with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> = p_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1075" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1075"></td>
        <td id="LC1075" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1076" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1076"></td>
        <td id="LC1076" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1077" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1077"></td>
        <td id="LC1077" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">More general explicit cases of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(C)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with parametrization by Darboux coordinates for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>C = <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G=<span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> case are discussed in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FrassekPestun}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1078" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1078"></td>
        <td id="LC1078" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1079" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1079"></td>
        <td id="LC1079" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\subsection</span>{Symplectic Structures for General <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{general_symplectic_sec}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1080" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1080"></td>
        <td id="LC1080" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We begin analysis of the general case by briefly discussing the holomorphic symplectic structure on the moduli space of periodic monopoles on $\bb{CP}^1$ following the work of Cherkis and Kapustin \cite{CherkisKapustin1, CherkisKapustin3}.  This structure arises from the description we gave as a hyperk\&quot;ahler quotient.  To describe it specifically, let $\delta^{(1)} \mc A$ and $\delta^{(2)} \mc A$ be two tangent vectors at $(\bo P, \mc A)$ to the moduli space of monopoles.  Recall that $\mc A$ denotes the combination $\nabla_t - i\Phi \d t$.  Choose representatives for these two tangent vectors of the form $\alpha_i$ and $\alpha&#39;_i$ respectively  in the \v Cech resolution we described above.  Then we can write the holomorphic symplectic form coming from the hyperk\&quot;ahler reduction in terms of the symplectic pairing on the infinite-dimensional vector space $\mc V$, which is given by the Killing form $\kappa$ on $\gg$ along with the wedge pairing of differential forms.  So summing over the local patches in our \v Cech resolution we can write it as</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1081" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1081"></td>
        <td id="LC1081" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1082" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1082"></td>
        <td id="LC1082" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{M} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{z} <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
