        <td id="L1083" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1083"></td>
        <td id="LC1083" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^k <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{U_i <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i, <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{z} <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t</td>

We&#39;ll discuss this further in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{hyperkahler_section}</td>
      </tr>

        <td id="L1086" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1086"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1087" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1087"></td>
        <td id="LC1087" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Our goal in this section will be describe a symplectic structure on the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles -- the rational analogue of Hurtubise and Markman&#39;s symplectic structure -- and then prove that it&#39;s equivalent to this symplectic form under the equivalence between multiplicative Higgs bundles and periodic monopoles.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1088" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1088"></td>

</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1089" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1089"></td>

      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1090" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1090"></td>
        <td id="LC1090" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">From now on we&#39;ll write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> - , - <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to denote the residue pairing between elements of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  That is, </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1091" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1091"></td>
        <td id="LC1091" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> g_1, g_2 <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\oint</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(g_1, g_2).<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>

        <td id="L1094" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1094"></td>
        <td id="LC1094" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{lemma} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{sym_nondegeneracy_lemma}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1095" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1095"></td>
        <td id="LC1095" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is a natural non-degenerate anti-symmetric pairing on the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In terms of our <span class="pl-c1">\v</span> Cech description it is described by the formula </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1096" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1096"></td>
        <td id="LC1096" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>((<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>), (<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i&#39;<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)) = <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> 12 <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_i <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i + <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_0)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i}, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i) <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i + <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_0)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i}, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>&#39;_i) <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1097" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1097"></td>
        <td id="LC1097" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where we use the Killing form to identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>&#39;_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued form, and where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the pullback along the right multiplication by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In this expression the sum is over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i=<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i=<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1098" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1098"></td>
        <td id="LC1098" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{lemma}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1099" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1099"></td>
        <td id="LC1099" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1100" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1100"></td>
        <td id="LC1100" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1101" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1101"></td>
        <td id="LC1101" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">How should we think about this structure?  There&#39;s an intuitive description, just as one sees in Hurtubise and Markman&#39;s elliptic moduli space.  The pairing is induced from the natural equivalence between the tangent and cotangent spaces of the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles as described in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{def_section}.  That is, there&#39;s a map of complexes of sheaves</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1102" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1102"></td>
        <td id="LC1102" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\xymatrix</span>{</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1103" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1103"></td>
        <td id="LC1103" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_{(P,g)})^*[2] <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{=}[r] <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d] &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\Big</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>^*_P(-D)[1] <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-c) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d]^{<span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span> <span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*} <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r]^{<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*} &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>^*_P <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-c)<span class="pl-c1">\Big</span>)<span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[d]^{<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g <span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>^{-1}} <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1104" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1104"></td>
        <td id="LC1104" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> F^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_{(P,g)} <span class="pl-c1">\ar@</span>{=}[r] &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\Big</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P[1] <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-c) <span class="pl-c1">\ar</span>[r]^{<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g} &amp;<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P(D) <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(-c)<span class="pl-c1">\Big</span>)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1105" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1105"></td>
        <td id="LC1105" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">}<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1106" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1106"></td>
        <td id="LC1106" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where here <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> denotes the isomorphism from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_P <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>^*_P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> induced by the Killing form.  The top line is the Serre dual complex to the bottom line; note that the incorporation of the framing was necessary for this to be the case (that is, we&#39;re using the relative Calabi-Yau structure on the pair <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, c)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).  Taking 0th hypercohomology we obtain a map from the cotangent space to the tangent space of our moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1107" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1107"></td>
        <td id="LC1107" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1108" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1108"></td>
        <td id="LC1108" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1109" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1109"></td>
        <td id="LC1109" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1110" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1110"></td>
        <td id="LC1110" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">At this point we will not prove that the pairing is a symplectic structure: we will not verify the Jacobi identity.  While we expect that it is possible to prove this directly using the techniques of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 5]{HurtubiseMarkman}, instead we&#39;ll see this below by proving that the pairing coincides with the symplectic pairing on the moduli space of periodic monopoles.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1111" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1111"></td>
        <td id="LC1111" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1112" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1112"></td>
        <td id="LC1112" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1113" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1113"></td>
        <td id="LC1113" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1114" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1114"></td>
        <td id="LC1114" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We need only verify that the pairing described is non-degenerate.  It suffices to check non-degeneracy for each individual summand, i.e. that for fixed <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, given <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if the expression <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i}, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>&#39;_i) <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> vanishes for all <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>&#39;_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> then <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (and the same with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> interchanged).  This is immediate because the residue pairing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> - , - <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is non-degenerate and the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an isomorphism on the open set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1115" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1115"></td>
        <td id="LC1115" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1116" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1116"></td>
        <td id="LC1116" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1117" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1117"></td>
        <td id="LC1117" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1118" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1118"></td>
        <td id="LC1118" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">If we do not fix local data at the punctures, the full moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, or indeed the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr,sing}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with arbitrary singularities, will have an ind-Poisson structure, analogous to the ind-Poisson structure in the elliptic moduli space of Hurtubise and Markman.  One uses the filtration discussed in Remark <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{ind_structure_remark} in order to define this structure: one needs to check that the moduli space  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D, <span class="pl-c1">\preceq</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is Poisson, and that the inclusion of the symplectic moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a Poisson map.  We won&#39;t discuss this in any more detail here, except to remark that this should follow using the techniques of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 7]{HurtubiseMarkman}.  We will, however, discuss the close relationship between this Poisson structure and the rational Poisson Lie group, and the consequences for quantization, in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{quantization_section}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1119" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1119"></td>
        <td id="LC1119" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1120" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1120"></td>
        <td id="LC1120" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1121" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1121"></td>
        <td id="LC1121" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In fact the moduli space is not only symplectic, but the total space of a completely integrable system -- the multiplicative Hitchin system described in Definition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{mult_Hitchin_system_def}.  We already know that the generic fibers are half-dimensional tori, it remains to verify that they&#39;re isotropic.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1122" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1122"></td>
        <td id="LC1122" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1123" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1123"></td>
        <td id="LC1123" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{prop} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Hitchin_isotropic_prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1124" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1124"></td>
        <td id="LC1124" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Generic fibers of the multiplicative Hitchin fibration, in the rational case, are isotropic.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1125" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1125"></td>
        <td id="LC1125" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1126" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1126"></td>
        <td id="LC1126" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1127" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1127"></td>
        <td id="LC1127" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1128" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1128"></td>
        <td id="LC1128" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to check this we need to describe the subspace of the tangent space to the moduli space $\mhiggs^\fr_G(C,D,\omega^\vee)$ at a point $(P,g)$ tangent to the Hitchin fiber in our \v Cech description.  Recall that the tangent space to $\mhiggs^\fr_G(C,D,\omega^\vee)$ can be identified as the space of \v Cech cocycles $(\alpha_0, \{\alpha_i\}, \alpha_\infty, \{\beta_i\}, \beta_\infty)$, where in particular the $\beta_i$ and $\beta_\infty$ are local sections of the adjoint bundle $\gg_P$.  We will show that, for a \v Cech cocycle lying tangent to the Hitchin fiber, the elements $\beta_i, \beta_\infty$ must be valued in the associated bundle of centralizers $\mf c_g$ of $g$.  Having established this the claim follows because the operator $\Ad_g$, and therefore the operator $(\Ad_g^*)^{-1}$, acts trivially on the centralizer of $g$.  Replacing this operator with the identity in our expression for the symplectic form from Lemma \ref{sym_nondegeneracy_lemma} results in a symmetric expression.  Since it&#39;s also antisymmetric, it must vanish, which implies the desired isotropic condition.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1129" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1129"></td>
        <td id="LC1129" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1130" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1130"></td>
        <td id="LC1130" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">So it remains to establish this restriction on tangent vectors to the Hitchin fiber.  Note that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> lies in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> c_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if and only if <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  If the derivative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the multiplicative Hitchin map annihilates a cocycle, then in particular the elements <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are functions without poles at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Indeed, the cocycle condition implies that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has the same residue as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> applied to a regular function, in particular, by the genericity assumption, its residue is regular semisimple.  On the other hand, being in the kernel of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> means vanishing under the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mf</span> t(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- the two conditions together implies that the simple pole of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has zero residue.  That means that the tangent vectors to the Hitchin fiber -- which are annihilated by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- are cohomologous to cocycles with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as required.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1131" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1131"></td>
        <td id="LC1131" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1132" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1132"></td>
        <td id="LC1132" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1133" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1133"></td>
        <td id="LC1133" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll now begin the comparison between the pairing described above and the symplectic structure on the moduli space of periodic monopoles.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1134" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1134"></td>
        <td id="LC1134" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1135" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1135"></td>
        <td id="LC1135" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{prop} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{qconn_symp_description}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1136" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1136"></td>
        <td id="LC1136" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The non-degenerate pairing on the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles can be written in the form</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1137" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1137"></td>
        <td id="LC1137" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{equation}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1138" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1138"></td>
        <td id="LC1138" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{eq:resid}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1139" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1139"></td>
        <td id="LC1139" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g&#39;) = <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^d <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> b_i^L g^{-1}, b^{&#39;R}_i g^{-1} <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1140" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1140"></td>
        <td id="LC1140" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{equation}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1141" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1141"></td>
        <td id="LC1141" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is represented on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by a pair <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(b^L, b^R) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Here and throughout the notation ``<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>- (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>&#39;&#39; denotes antisymmetrization.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1142" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1142"></td>
        <td id="LC1142" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1143" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1143"></td>
        <td id="LC1143" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1144" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1144"></td>
        <td id="LC1144" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1145" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1145"></td>
        <td id="LC1145" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> Specify a representative cocycle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>, <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for an element of the first <span class="pl-c1">\v</span> Cech cohomology group. By addition of a coboundary we can assume that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and to force <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to land in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[[z]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to land in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z^{-1}<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[[z]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We have now fixed a representative cocycle -- there&#39;s no further gauge freedom.  Ignoring the factor at infinity -- since after we add these coboundaries the residue pairing there vanishes -- the pairing we end up with looks like </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1146" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1146"></td>
        <td id="LC1146" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1147" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1147"></td>
        <td id="LC1147" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g&#39;) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> 12 <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^d <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i + <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_0)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i},<span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^* (<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}( <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>_i) <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - ((<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> (<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;,<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>&#39;)<span class="pl-c1">\\</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1148" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1148"></td>
        <td id="LC1148" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> 12 <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^d <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i + <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_0)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i}, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i - <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_0)) <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - (<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span> <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;)<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1149" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1149"></td>
        <td id="LC1149" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> 12 <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^d <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i}, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i)|_{U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i}) <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - (<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span> <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1150" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1150"></td>
        <td id="LC1150" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1151" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1151"></td>
        <td id="LC1151" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1152" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1152"></td>
        <td id="LC1152" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can compute the composite operator <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*)^{-1}<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ad}(P)(U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  It&#39;s given by the inverse of the operator <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g<span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which sends a pair <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(b^L, b^R) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ad}(P)(U^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_i)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(b^L - b^R, b^R - b^L) <span class="pl-c1">\sim</span> (b^L + g^{-1} b^L g, b^R - g b^R g^{-1})<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Denote this by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>((<span class="pl-c1">1</span>+A_g)b^L,(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>-A_{g^{-1}})b^R)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can describe the inverse using the expansion <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>+A_g)^{-1} = <span class="pl-c1">1</span> - A_g + A_g^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> + <span class="pl-c1">\cdots</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  After applying our gauge transformation above the remaining degree of freedom in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is its <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> term.  Each time we apply <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> it raises the order in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of this term by one, so only the linear summand <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>-A_g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>+A_g)^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> contributes to the residue pairing.  In the pairing we need to use the invariant pairing on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>((z)) <span class="pl-c1">\oplus</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>((z))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that vanishes on the subalgebra spanned by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(X, A_g(X))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so we take the difference of the residue / Killing form pairings on the two summands.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1153" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1153"></td>
        <td id="LC1153" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1154" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1154"></td>
        <td id="LC1154" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g&#39;) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> 12 <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^d  - <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*A_g b^{&#39;L}_i, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*b^{R}_i <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*b^{&#39;L}_i, <span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_g^*A_{g^{-1}}b^{R}_i <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>- (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1155" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1155"></td>
        <td id="LC1155" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1}^d <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span> b^L_ig^{-1}, b^{&#39;R}_i g^{-1} <span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span>  - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1156" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1156"></td>
        <td id="LC1156" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1157" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1157"></td>
        <td id="LC1157" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">using cyclic invariant to identify the two terms. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1158" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1158"></td>
        <td id="LC1158" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1159" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1159"></td>
        <td id="LC1159" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1160" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1160"></td>
        <td id="LC1160" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll use this description of the pairing to compare our symplectic structure with the Poisson structure of the rational Poisson Lie group in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{quantization_section}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1161" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1161"></td>
        <td id="LC1161" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1162" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1162"></td>
        <td id="LC1162" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can now establish our main result.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1163" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1163"></td>
        <td id="LC1163" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{symplectic_comparison_thm}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1164" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1164"></td>
        <td id="LC1164" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The symplectic structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the pullback of the non-degenerate pairing on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> coincide.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1165" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1165"></td>
        <td id="LC1165" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1166" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1166"></td>
        <td id="LC1166" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1167" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1167"></td>
        <td id="LC1167" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1168" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1168"></td>
        <td id="LC1168" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is straightforward now, by combining the two local descriptions of the symplectic structure on monopoles and multiplicative Higgs bundles on a neighborhood of a puncture with the description in Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{local_derivative_description_prop}.  So, let us begin by taking the symplectic form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and evaluating it at the image under <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of two elements <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i, <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i) = (<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i), <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i&#39;))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let us write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_i(<span class="pl-c1">0</span>) = b_i^L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_i(<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>) = b_i^R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for brevity.  Likewise for consistency with the calculations above let us denote the image <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>H(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the holonomy map by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1169" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1169"></td>
        <td id="LC1169" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1170" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1170"></td>
        <td id="LC1170" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">According to Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{local_derivative_description_prop} we have</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1171" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1171"></td>
        <td id="LC1171" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1172" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1172"></td>
        <td id="LC1172" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i), <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i&#39;)) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i)), <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i&#39;))) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1173" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1173"></td>
        <td id="LC1173" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}(b_i^Rg - gb_i^L,b_i^{&#39;R}g - gb_i^{&#39;L}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1174" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1174"></td>
        <td id="LC1174" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1175" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1175"></td>
        <td id="LC1175" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can write this in terms of a pairing on the bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Represent the class <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_i^Rg - gb_i^L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by the pair <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(b_i^Rg, -gb_i^L)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Then applying the description of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> provided by Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{qconn_symp_description} we have</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1176" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1176"></td>
        <td id="LC1176" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1177" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1177"></td>
        <td id="LC1177" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i), <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> H(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i&#39;)) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}}((b_i^Rg, -gb_i^L),(b_i^{&#39;R}g, -gb_i^{&#39;L})) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1178" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1178"></td>
        <td id="LC1178" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= - <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span>  b_i^R , g b_i&#39;^L g^{-1}<span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1179" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1179"></td>
        <td id="LC1179" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1180" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1180"></td>
        <td id="LC1180" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the remaining terms are killed by the antisymmetrization.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1181" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1181"></td>
        <td id="LC1181" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1182" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1182"></td>
        <td id="LC1182" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">On the other hand, we can evaluate the pairing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Mon}}(<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i,<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i) = <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Mon}}(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i),<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i&#39;))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> via integration by parts. We&#39;ll compute the symplectic pairing for the full <span class="pl-c1">\v</span> Cech complex, but it will split into a sum over open sets <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The result is that </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1183" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1183"></td>
        <td id="LC1183" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1184" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1184"></td>
        <td id="LC1184" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Mon}}(<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=0,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k,<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{U_i} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i) <span class="pl-c1">\wedge</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b_i&#39;)) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)<span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1185" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1185"></td>
        <td id="LC1185" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k,<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\dd</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D_i <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> [0,2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>]} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b_i - b_0, <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}(b&#39;_i)) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1186" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1186"></td>
        <td id="LC1186" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1187" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1187"></td>
        <td id="LC1187" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">using here the fact that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}}b_i = <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}} b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i <span class="pl-c1">\cap</span> U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mon}} b_i(t) = <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> when <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t = <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  By Stokes&#39; theorem we then have</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1188" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1188"></td>
        <td id="LC1188" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1189" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1189"></td>
        <td id="LC1189" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Mon}}(<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>)&amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k,<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\oint</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\dd</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D_i} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b_i^R - b_0^R, b_i^{&#39;R}) - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b_i^L - b_0^L, b_i^{&#39;L}) - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1190" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1190"></td>
        <td id="LC1190" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k,<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\oint</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\dd</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D_i} - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b_0^R, b_i^{&#39;R}) + <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b_0^L, b_i^{&#39;L}) - (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1191" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1191"></td>
        <td id="LC1191" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1192" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1192"></td>
        <td id="LC1192" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Pick out the summand corresponding to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Choose our potentials so that on the boundary <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\dd</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> D_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we have <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>^L = b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>^{&#39;L} = <span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can do this by setting <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b^{R} = <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g g^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is non-singular on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This choice means that on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> <span class="pl-c1">\cap</span> U_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, since <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> g  = b_{i} ^R g - g b_i^L = b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>^{R} g <span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we can make the identification <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span> b_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>^{R} = b_{i}^{R} - g b_{i}^{L} g^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Therefore</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1193" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1193"></td>
        <td id="LC1193" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Mon}}(<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>&#39;_i<span class="pl-cce">\}</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{i=1,<span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>,k,<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\langle</span>(g b_i^{L} g^{-1}, b_i^{&#39;R}<span class="pl-c1">\rangle</span> <span class="pl-c1">\quad</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\quad</span>  (b <span class="pl-c1">\leftrightarrow</span> b&#39;)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1194" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1194"></td>
        <td id="LC1194" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">agreeing with the expression coming from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{mHiggs}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1195" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1195"></td>
        <td id="LC1195" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1196" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1196"></td>
        <td id="LC1196" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1197" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1197"></td>
        <td id="LC1197" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In particular the non-degenerate pairing on the multiplicative Higgs moduli space is determined by a closed 2-form, and the multiplicative Hitchin fibers are Lagrangian.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1198" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1198"></td>
        <td id="LC1198" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1199" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1199"></td>
        <td id="LC1199" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{corollary}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1200" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1200"></td>
        <td id="LC1200" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has the structure of a completely integrable system.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1201" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1201"></td>
        <td id="LC1201" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{corollary}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1202" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1202"></td>
        <td id="LC1202" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1203" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1203"></td>
        <td id="LC1203" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{Hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler Structures} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{hyperkahler_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1204" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1204"></td>
        <td id="LC1204" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The results of the previous section imply that the symplectic structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> extends canonically to a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure.  In this section we&#39;ll compare the twistor rotation with the deformation to the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections. We&#39;ll show that in an appropriate limit passing to a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the twistor sphere we obtain a complex manifold equivalent to the moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-connections as a deformation of the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1205" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1205"></td>
        <td id="LC1205" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1206" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1206"></td>
        <td id="LC1206" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us begin by describing the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure on the moduli space of periodic monopoles and how the holomorphic symplectic structure varies under rotation in the twistor sphere.  We&#39;ll begin by recalling that the moduli space of periodic monopoles can be described as a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler quotient as in the work of Atiyah and Hitchin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{AtiyahHitchin}.  In a context with more general boundary data at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> this was demonstrated by Cherkis and Kapustin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{CherkisKapustin3} for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SU</span>(<span class="pl-c1">2</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, see also Foscolo <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FoscoloDef}[Theorem 7.12].  In the case of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a fixed framing the analysis is much easier.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1207" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1207"></td>
        <td id="LC1207" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1208" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1208"></td>
        <td id="LC1208" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Recall from Definition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{monopole_moduli_def} that the moduli space of periodic monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a fixed framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and fixed Dirac singularities can be described as the quotient </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1209" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1209"></td>
        <td id="LC1209" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^1_R, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) = <span class="pl-c1">\mu</span>^{-1}(0)/<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G,<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1210" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1210"></td>
        <td id="LC1210" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1211" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1211"></td>
        <td id="LC1211" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1212" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1212"></td>
        <td id="LC1212" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of fields is the space of pairs <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consisting of framed connections <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on the trivial principal <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a section of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> vanishing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the pair <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a Dirac singularity with charge <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at each point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z_i,t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\{</span>t_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1213" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1213"></td>
        <td id="LC1213" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mu</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> V <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R; (<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P})/<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the map sending a monopole <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(A, <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued 1-form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ast</span> F_A - <span class="pl-c1">\d</span>_A <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> vanishing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1214" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1214"></td>
        <td id="LC1214" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of gauge transformations consists of automorphisms of the trivial bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bo</span> P<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fixing the framing.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1215" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1215"></td>
        <td id="LC1215" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{itemize}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1216" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1216"></td>
        <td id="LC1216" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1217" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1217"></td>
        <td id="LC1217" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This is an instance of hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler reduction.  Indeed the infinite-dimensional space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> V<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> admits a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure with symplectic forms defined by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1218" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1218"></td>
        <td id="LC1218" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_i((A,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>),(A&#39;,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>&#39;)) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^1_R} <span class="pl-c1">\left</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(A_i,<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>&#39;) - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span>, A_i&#39;) + <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{j,k=1,2,3} <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>_{ijk} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(A_j,A&#39;_k)<span class="pl-c1">\right</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> x <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> y <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t, <span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1219" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1219"></td>
        <td id="LC1219" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i=<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,<span class="pl-c1">2</span>,<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be written as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t + A_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> x + A_<span class="pl-c1">3</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> y<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with respect to a choice <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z = <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> (x + iy)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of meromorphic volume form on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a second order pole at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This descends to a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure on the quotient; see <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 1.4.2]{FoscoloThesis}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1220" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1220"></td>
        <td id="LC1220" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1221" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1221"></td>
        <td id="LC1221" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us restrict to the case where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for now.  Consider the holomorphic symplectic structure <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> + i <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We can alternatively write the formula above for this choice of holomorphic symplectic structure in the form</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1222" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1222"></td>
        <td id="LC1222" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>((A_0, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A), (A_0&#39;, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A&#39;)) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1_R} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(A_0, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A&#39;) - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, A_0&#39;) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> x <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> y <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t,<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1223" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1223"></td>
        <td id="LC1223" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">0</span> = A_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> + i A_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A = A_<span class="pl-c1">1</span> - i <span class="pl-c1">\Phi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1224" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1224"></td>
        <td id="LC1224" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1225" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1225"></td>
        <td id="LC1225" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1226" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1226"></td>
        <td id="LC1226" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can compare this to the expression described at the beginning of Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{general_symplectic_sec}. Indeed, up to a factor of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we can rewrite this expression as</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1227" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1227"></td>
        <td id="LC1227" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>((A_0, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A), (A_0&#39;, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A&#39;)) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1_R} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(A_0<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z + <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t, A_0&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z + <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t) <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ol</span>{z}.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1228" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1228"></td>
        <td id="LC1228" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This expression agrees with the symplectic pairing on monopoles in Section <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{general_symplectic_sec} as a pairing of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued 1-forms on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which are holomorphic in the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-direction, where we set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A = A_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z + <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1229" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1229"></td>
        <td id="LC1229" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1230" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1230"></td>
        <td id="LC1230" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1231" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1231"></td>
        <td id="LC1231" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This description for the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler structure also tells us clearly what happens when we perform a rotation in the twistor sphere.  The following statement follows by identifying the holomorphic symplectic structure at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the twistor sphere by applying the corresponding rotation in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the coordinates <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>x<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the expression for the holomorphic symplectic structure at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Note that when we calculate the symplectic form as an integral as above, it&#39;s enough to take the integral over just <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> instead of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1232" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1232"></td>
        <td id="LC1232" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1233" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1233"></td>
