        <td id="LC1233" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Notationally, from now on we&#39;ll write the holomorphic symplectic pairing in the abbreviated form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(A_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A&#39;) - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, A_<span class="pl-c1">0</span>&#39;) = <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and we&#39;ll write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the volume form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\d</span> x <span class="pl-c1">\wedge</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> y <span class="pl-c1">\wedge</span> <span class="pl-c1">\d</span> t<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1234" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1234"></td>
        <td id="LC1234" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1235" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1235"></td>
        <td id="LC1235" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1236" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1236"></td>
        <td id="LC1236" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be a point in the twistor sphere.  The holomorphic symplectic form on the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of periodic monopoles is given by the formula </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1237" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1237"></td>
        <td id="LC1237" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^2 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^1_R} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span>),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1238" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1238"></td>
        <td id="LC1238" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where we identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with an element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">3</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and apply this rotation to the volume form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Equivalently we can identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the quotient <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">3</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the rank one lattice <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-c1">\}</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R<span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and identify the rotated holomorphic symplectic form with </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1239" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1239"></td>
        <td id="LC1239" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(L))} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1240" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1240"></td>
        <td id="LC1240" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{prop}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1241" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1241"></td>
        <td id="LC1241" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1242" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1242"></td>
        <td id="LC1242" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, we&#39;ll perform our identification of the twistor deformation on the multiplicative Higgs side by rewriting this twistor rotation in a somewhat different way in the large <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> limit.  In this limit we can identify the twistor rotation with the deformation obtained by replacing the product <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the product twisted by an automorphism of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  More precisely, the rotated symplectic structure can then be described in the following way.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1243" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1243"></td>
        <td id="LC1243" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1244" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1244"></td>
        <td id="LC1244" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{HK_rotation_thm}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1245" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1245"></td>
        <td id="LC1245" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\left</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-c1">\right</span>)_{<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>,R}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the family of complex manifolds obtained by pulling back the holomorphic symplectic structure <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>,R}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ps},<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the twistor sphere.  In the limit where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span> R = <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fixed this complex structure coincides with the complex structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\epsconn</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, in the sense that the complex structures converge pointwise over the tangent bundle to the moduli space of monopoles. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1246" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1246"></td>
        <td id="LC1246" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1247" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1247"></td>
        <td id="LC1247" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1248" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1248"></td>
        <td id="LC1248" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1249" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1249"></td>
        <td id="LC1249" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">First let us note that the 3-manifolds <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for varying values of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are all diffeomorphic (via a diffeomorphism fixing the circle at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).  This means that we can identify the moduli spaces in question as smooth manifolds by choosing such a diffeomorphism.  Then, according to Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{monopole_qconn_comparison_thm} it&#39;s enough to show that the complex structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> converges to the complex structure on the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-deformation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ps},<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The key observation that we&#39;ll use is that, fixing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span> R = <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we can identify the rotated lattice with a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{sheared} lattice.  Namely, when we rotate the rank one lattice <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>L_{R,0} = (<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">0</span>,<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R)<span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we obtain the lattice</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1250" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1250"></td>
        <td id="LC1250" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(L_{R,0}) = <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2} (<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Re}(<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>), <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Im}(<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>), 2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R (1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2) )<span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1251" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1251"></td>
        <td id="LC1251" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We can view the quotient of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by the rotated lattice as a sheared lattice with different radius and shear.  Specifically, we identify</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1252" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1252"></td>
        <td id="LC1252" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3 / <span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(L_{R,0}) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^2 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}} S^1_{R <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}}.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1253" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1253"></td>
        <td id="LC1253" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1254" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1254"></td>
        <td id="LC1254" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In order to identify the desired complex structures it&#39;s enough to identify the full family of symplectic structures on the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-deformation with the appropriately rotated family of symplectic structures without deforming.  So, if we apply the twistor rotation by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the holomorphic symplectic structure <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">2</span> + i<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">3</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (the argument will be identical for the other points in the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> family of holomorphic symplectic structures) we obtain the pairing</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1255" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1255"></td>
        <td id="LC1255" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(L_{R,0}))} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1256" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1256"></td>
        <td id="LC1256" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">On the other hand we can identify the holomorphic symplectic structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ps},<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1257" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1257"></td>
        <td id="LC1257" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) = <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(L_{R,<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>})} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1258" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1258"></td>
        <td id="LC1258" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In particular, by tuning the radius and the shear parameter the above calculation means there&#39;s a hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler equivalence between the moduli spaces <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ps,fr}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_R,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- after rotating the twistor sphere by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mon</span>_G^{<span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{ps},<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}} S^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_{R <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}},D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1259" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1259"></td>
        <td id="LC1259" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1260" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1260"></td>
        <td id="LC1260" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, let us consider the large <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> limit.  We&#39;d like to note that the following difference of symplectic pairings converges to zero pointwise as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1261" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1261"></td>
        <td id="LC1261" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span> <span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(L_{R <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2},<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}})} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(L_{R,<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>})} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> <span class="pl-c1">\right</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span>.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1262" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1262"></td>
        <td id="LC1262" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Rescaling the radii of the circles only rescales the pairing by an overall constant, so we can rewrite this as </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1263" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1263"></td>
        <td id="LC1263" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span> R<span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2} <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(L_{1,<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}})} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\RR</span>^3/(L_{1,<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>})} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> <span class="pl-c1">\right</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span><span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1264" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1264"></td>
        <td id="LC1264" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">in which we recall that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> {2<span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> R}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Write <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(i)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the image of the deformation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(i)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the diffeomorphism induced by identifying the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted product with the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted product, so <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(i)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>(z,t) = <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(i)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A(z-<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2},t)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Note that when we perform the integral the pairing between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the pairing between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)}<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> coincide.  In other words, our difference of pairings becomes</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1265" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1265"></td>
        <td id="LC1265" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*} </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1266" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1266"></td>
        <td id="LC1266" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;R<span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^1_1} <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A_<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>)  -  <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> <span class="pl-c1">\right</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1267" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1267"></td>
        <td id="LC1267" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\quad</span> = R <span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> {1-|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2}{1+|<span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span>|^2} - 1 <span class="pl-c1">\right\rvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^1_1} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> <span class="pl-c1">\right</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1268" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1268"></td>
        <td id="LC1268" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\quad</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert\frac</span> {2R |<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>|^2}{4 <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span>^2 R^2 + |<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span>|^2} <span class="pl-c1">\right</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\left\lvert</span> <span class="pl-c1">\int</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1 <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\eps</span> S^1_1} <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(1)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A, <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>^{(2)} <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> A) <span class="pl-c1">\dvol</span> <span class="pl-c1">\right</span> <span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1269" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1269"></td>
        <td id="LC1269" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1270" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1270"></td>
        <td id="LC1270" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This converges to zero pointwise as <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The same calculation proves convergence for the other symplectic structures in the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler family, and therefore convergence for the difference of the two complex structures.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1271" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1271"></td>
        <td id="LC1271" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1272" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1272"></td>
        <td id="LC1272" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1273" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1273"></td>
        <td id="LC1273" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{example} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Nahm_example}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1274" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1274"></td>
        <td id="LC1274" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the case where the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G=<span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> it&#39;s possible to describe the multiplicative Hitchin system on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in terms of an <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{ordinary} Hitchin system on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, but for a different group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and with different singularity data.  This relationship is given by the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Nahm transform}.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1275" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1275"></td>
        <td id="LC1275" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1276" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1276"></td>
        <td id="LC1276" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us give an informal explanation.  From a gauge-theoretic point of view, the Nahm transform arises from the Fourier-Mukai transform for anti-self-dual connections on a 4-torus $T$, relating an of ASD connection on a vector bundle to an ASD connection on the bundle of kernels for the associated Dirac operator, a vector bundle on the dual torus $T^\vee$ (see the book of Donaldson--Kronheimer \cite[Section 3.2]{DonaldsonKronheimer}).  There is a Nahm transform relating the ordinary Hitchin system to the moduli space of periodic monopoles obtained in an appropriate limit: consider the torus $T = S^1_{r_1} \times S^1_{r_2} \times S^1_{r_3} \times S^1_{R}$.  The moduli space of periodic monopoles on $\CC$ arises in the limit where $r_1$ and $r_2$ go to $\infty$ and $r_3$ goes to zero.  On the other hand, the Hitchin system on $\CC^\times$ arises in the dual limit where $r_1$ and $r_2$ go to zero and $r_3$ goes to $\infty$.  The Nahm transform in this setting -- i.e. for periodic monopoles -- was developed by Cherkis and Kapustin \cite{CherkisKapustin2}, and worked out in detail in the case $n=2$ (they also give a brane description of the transform: see \cite[Section 2]{CherkisKapustin2}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1277" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1277"></td>
        <td id="LC1277" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1278" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1278"></td>
        <td id="LC1278" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One then has to match up the singularity data.  In brief, the multiplicative Hitchin system for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> singularities at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, z_k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is equivalent to the ordinary Hitchin system on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>_k<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> regular singularities, which residues determined by the original positions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and positions determined by the original local data <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We refer to <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 7.1]{NekrasovPestun} for more details.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1279" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1279"></td>
        <td id="LC1279" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1280" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1280"></td>
        <td id="LC1280" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the example where we have the Nahm transform available, we conjecture that the multiplicative geometric Langlands equivalence recovers the ordinary geometric Langlands equivalence with tame ramification.  That is, we expect the following.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1281" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1281"></td>
        <td id="LC1281" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1282" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1282"></td>
        <td id="LC1282" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{claim}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1283" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1283"></td>
        <td id="LC1283" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Under the Nahm transform, Pseudo-Conjecture <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{multLanglands} in the rational case for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\GL</span>(n)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> becomes the ordinary geometric Langlands conjecture on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with tame ramification.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1284" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1284"></td>
        <td id="LC1284" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{claim}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1285" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1285"></td>
        <td id="LC1285" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{example}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1286" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1286"></td>
        <td id="LC1286" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1287" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1287"></td>
        <td id="LC1287" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1288" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1288"></td>
        <td id="LC1288" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  The limit <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>R <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">2</span> <span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\zeta</span> R = <span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> appearing in the hyperk<span class="pl-cce">\&quot;</span>ahler rotation</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1289" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1289"></td>
        <td id="LC1289" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{HK_rotation_thm} was first suggested by Gaiotto <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GaiottoTBA} on the other side of the Nahm transform.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1290" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1290"></td>
        <td id="LC1290" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1291" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1291"></td>
        <td id="LC1291" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1292" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1292"></td>
        <td id="LC1292" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{The Rational Poisson Lie Group and the Yangian} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{quantization_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1293" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1293"></td>
        <td id="LC1293" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let us proceed by discussing the connection between the symplectic structure on the moduli space of multiplicative Higgs bundles in the rational case and the rational Poisson Lie group.  This connection should be compared to the connection between the elliptic moduli space and the elliptic quantum group in the work of Hurtubise and Markman <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Theorem 9.1]{HurtubiseMarkman}.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1294" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1294"></td>
        <td id="LC1294" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1295" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1295"></td>
        <td id="LC1295" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Consider the infinite-type moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr,sing}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of multiplicative Higgs bundles with arbitrary singularities.  There is a map</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1296" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1296"></td>
        <td id="LC1296" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr,sing}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G_1[[z^{-1}]],<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1297" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1297"></td>
        <td id="LC1297" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">defined by restricting a multiplicative Higgs bundle to a formal neighborhood of infinity.  In particular we can restrict <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to any of the finite-dimensional subspaces <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (the symplectic leaves).  Here the notation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> denotes Taylor series in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with constant term 1.  Recall that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a Poisson Lie group, with Poisson structure defined by the Manin triple <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(G(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>), G[[z]], G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (see <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Shapiro, Williams}).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1298" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1298"></td>
        <td id="LC1298" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1299" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1299"></td>
        <td id="LC1299" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The Poisson Lie group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has the structure of an ind-scheme using the filtration where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> consists of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued polynomials in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with identity constant term and where the matrix elements in a fixed faithful representation have degree at most <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  When we talk about the Poisson algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of regular functions on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we are therefore referring to the limit over <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\ge</span> 0}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the finitely generated algebras <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]_n)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Due to the condition on the constant term the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is nilpotent, which means we can identify its algebra of functions with the algebra of functions on the Lie algebra.  That is:</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1300" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1300"></td>
        <td id="LC1300" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1301" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1301"></td>
        <td id="LC1301" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_1[[z^{-1}]]) &amp;= <span class="pl-c1">\underset</span> n <span class="pl-c1">\lim</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_1[[z^{-1}]]_n) <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1302" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1302"></td>
        <td id="LC1302" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">&amp;<span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\underset</span> n <span class="pl-c1">\lim</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sym</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_1^*[[z^{-1}]]_n).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1303" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1303"></td>
        <td id="LC1303" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{align*}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1304" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1304"></td>
        <td id="LC1304" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The Poisson bracket is compatible with this filtration, in the sense that it defines a map </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1305" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1305"></td>
        <td id="LC1305" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[\{</span>,<span class="pl-cce">\}</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_1[[z^{-1}]]_m) <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_1[[z^{-1}]]_n) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_1[[z^{-1}]]_{m+n})<span class="pl-cce">\]</span> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1306" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1306"></td>
        <td id="LC1306" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1307" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1307"></td>
        <td id="LC1307" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1308" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1308"></td>
        <td id="LC1308" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Poisson_Lie_Comparison_thm}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1309" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1309"></td>
        <td id="LC1309" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is Poisson.  That is, the pullback of the Poisson structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> coincides with the Poisson bracket on the space of regular functions on the moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of multiplicative Higgs bundles. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1310" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1310"></td>
        <td id="LC1310" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1311" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1311"></td>
        <td id="LC1311" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1312" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1312"></td>
        <td id="LC1312" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1313" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1313"></td>
        <td id="LC1313" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We just need to compute the pullback of the Poisson bracket on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This Poisson bracket is most easily described in terms of the rational <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-matrix: that is, we have an element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]] <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[w^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defined by the formula <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\frac</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span> {z-w}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Omega</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the quadratic Casimir element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The pairing defining the Poisson structure is given by contracting two cotangent vectors with the bivector field whose value at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g - <span class="pl-c1">\Ad</span>_g <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> <span class="pl-c1">1</span>)(r)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Concretely, given a pair of elements <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X&#39;<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the cotangent space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T^*_{G_1[[z^{-1}]], g}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, this computes the pairing</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1314" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1314"></td>
        <td id="LC1314" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>(X, X&#39;) <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> <span class="pl-c1">\int</span> <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(X, g X&#39; g^{-1}) - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(g X g^{-1},X&#39;)<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z,<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1315" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1315"></td>
        <td id="LC1315" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, for example, is identified with a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued meromorphic function on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, vanishing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, via pullback under the right multiplication by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> map.  Now, suppose the element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is in the image of the restriction map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for fixed local data <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Then we note that the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span>^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> sends a cotangent vector <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>X<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the meromorphic global section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(b^L, b^R) = (gX, -Xg)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the bundle <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g) <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> <span class="pl-c1">\ad</span>(g)^*<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> -- identifying the bundle with its dual using the invariant pairing  -- and so with this identification, our expression yields the formula</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1316" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1316"></td>
        <td id="LC1316" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>(X,X&#39;) <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> <span class="pl-c1">\int</span> <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b^Lg^{-1}, b^{&#39;R}g^{-1}) - <span class="pl-c1">\kappa</span>(b^{&#39;L}g^{-1}, b^{R}g^{-1})<span class="pl-c1">\d</span> z.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1317" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1317"></td>
        <td id="LC1317" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This recovers the expression given for the symplectic form in Proposition <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{qconn_symp_description} by applying the residue formula.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1318" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1318"></td>
        <td id="LC1318" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{proof}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1319" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1319"></td>
        <td id="LC1319" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1320" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1320"></td>
        <td id="LC1320" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{shapiro_leaves_remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1321" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1321"></td>
        <td id="LC1321" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It&#39;s instructive to compare this calculation with the work of Shapiro \cite{Shapiro} on symplectic leaves for the rational Poisson Lie group.  According to Shapiro, and for the group $G = \SL_n$, there are symplectic leaves in $G_1[[z^{-1}]]$ indexed by Smith normal forms, i.e. by a sequence $d_1, \ldots, d_n$ of polynomials where $d_i | d_{i+1}$ for each $i$.  This data is equivalent to a dominant coweight coloured divisor $(D,\omega^\vee)$ in the following way.  The data of the sequence of polynomials is equivalent to the data of an increasing sequence $(D_1, \ldots, D_n)$ of $n$ effective divisors in $\bb{CP}^1$ disjoint from $\infty$: the tuples of roots of the polynomials $d_i$.  Let $D = \{z_1, \ldots, z_k\}$ be the support of the largest divisor $D_n$, and for each $z_j$ let $\omega^\vee_{z_j} = (m_1, \ldots, m_n)$ be the dominant coweight where $m_i$ is the order of the root $z_j$ in the polynomial $d_i$.  The dominant coweight Shapiro refers to as the ``type&#39;&#39; of a leaf is, therefore, the sum of all these coweights.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1322" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1322"></td>
        <td id="LC1322" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1323" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1323"></td>
        <td id="LC1323" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">To be a little more precise, Shapiro proves that for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> these symplectic leaves span the Poisson subgroup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of elements that can be factorized as the product of a polynomial element in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[z^{-1}]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and a monic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued power series.  In fact, the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (for any group, not necessarily <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G = <span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) factors through the subgroup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: the Taylor expansion of all <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{rational} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> valued functions can be factorized in this way.  As a consequence, Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Poisson_Lie_Comparison_thm} implies that our symplectic leaves for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> agree with Shapiro&#39;s symplectic leaves.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1324" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1324"></td>
        <td id="LC1324" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1325" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1325"></td>
        <td id="LC1325" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1326" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1326"></td>
        <td id="LC1326" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This comparison has interesting consequences upon quantization.  The Poisson algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a well-studied quantization to the <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Yangian} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This is the unique Hopf algebra quantizing the algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[z])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with first order correction determined by the Lie bialgebra structure on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[z]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Recall that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>), <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[z], <span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a Manin triple, so the residue pairing on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(z)<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> induces an isomorphism between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and the dual to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[z]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and therefore a Lie cobracket on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[z]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The uniqueness of this quantization is a theorem due to Drinfeld {<span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Theorem 2]{DrinfeldQuantum1}}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1327" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1327"></td>
        <td id="LC1327" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1328" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1328"></td>
        <td id="LC1328" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1329" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1329"></td>
        <td id="LC1329" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Yangian} of the Lie algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the unique graded topological Hopf algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> which is a topologically free module over the graded ring <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>[[<span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has degree 1), so that when we set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>=<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> we recover <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>[[<span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>]]} <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span> <span class="pl-c1">\iso</span> U(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>[z])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as graded rings (where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has degree 1), and where the first order term in the comultiplication <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Delta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is determined by the cobracket <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\delta</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the sense that</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1330" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1330"></td>
        <td id="LC1330" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>^{-1}(<span class="pl-c1">\Delta</span>(f) - <span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\Delta</span>(f))) <span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ mod } <span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\delta</span>(f <span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ mod } <span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1331" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1331"></td>
        <td id="LC1331" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">for all elements <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>f <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Here <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the braiding automorphism of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)^{<span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> 2}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (i.e. <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>(f <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> g) = g <span class="pl-c1">\otimes</span> f<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1332" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1332"></td>
        <td id="LC1332" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1333" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1333"></td>
        <td id="LC1333" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1334" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1334"></td>
        <td id="LC1334" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">There is a very extensive literature on the Yangian and related quantum groups.  The general theory for quantization of Poisson Lie groups, including the Yangian, was developed by Etingof and Kazhdan <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{EtingofKazhdanIII}.  For more information we refer the reader to Chari and Pressley <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ChariPressley}, or for the Yangian specifically to the concise introduction in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 9]{CostelloYangian}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1335" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1335"></td>
        <td id="LC1335" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1336" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1336"></td>
        <td id="LC1336" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Likewise, we can study deformation quantization for the algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of functions on our symplectic moduli space.  This moduli space is, in particular, a smooth finite-dimensional Poisson manifold, so its algebra of functions can be quantized, for instance using Kontsevich&#39;s results on formality <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KontsevichQuantization}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1337" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1337"></td>
        <td id="LC1337" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1338" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1338"></td>
        <td id="LC1338" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1339" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1339"></td>
        <td id="LC1339" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The quantum algebra of functions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a choice of deformation quantization of the Poisson algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  That is, an associative <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>[[<span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebra where the antisymmetrization of the first order term in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the product recovers the Poisson bracket. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1340" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1340"></td>
        <td id="LC1340" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1341" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1341"></td>
        <td id="LC1341" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1342" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1342"></td>
        <td id="LC1342" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">While we have a Poisson morphism <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by Theorem <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{Poisson_Lie_Comparison_thm}, and therefore a map of Poisson algebras <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> there&#39;s no automatic guarantee that we can choose a quantization of the target admitting an algebra map from the Yangian quantizing this Poisson map -- one would need to verify the absence of an anomaly obstructing quantization.  There is however a natural model for this quantization, to a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-module,  constructed by Gerasimov, Kharchev, Lebedev and Oblezin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GKLO} (extending an earlier calculation <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{GKL} for <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span> = <span class="pl-c1">\gl</span>_n<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1343" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1343"></td>
        <td id="LC1343" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1344" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1344"></td>
        <td id="LC1344" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1345" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1345"></td>
        <td id="LC1345" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">For any reductive group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and any choice of local singularity data, the Poisson map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> quantizes to a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-module structure on an algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>_<span class="pl-c1">\hbar</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> quantizing the algebra of functions on the multiplicative Higgs moduli space.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1346" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1346"></td>
        <td id="LC1346" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{theorem}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1347" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1347"></td>
        <td id="LC1347" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1348" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1348"></td>
        <td id="LC1348" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This theorem is a direct consequence of the Gerasimov, Kharchev, Lebedev and Oblezin (GKLO) construction of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules whose classical limits are symplectic leaves in the rational Poisson Lie group.  They constructed these representations for any semisimple Lie algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>; they are indexed by the data of a dominant coweight-coloured divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  As in Shapiro, this data is encoded in the form of a set <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\nu</span>_{i,k}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of complex numbers, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> varies over simple roots of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>: the coweight at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>z <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is encoded by the vector <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(m_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, m_r)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>m_i = <span class="pl-c1">\lvert</span><span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\nu</span>_{i,k} = z<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-c1">\rvert</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let us denote this module by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M_{D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1349" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1349"></td>
        <td id="LC1349" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1350" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1350"></td>
        <td id="LC1350" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">GKLO discussed the classical limits of these modules <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M_{D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as symplectic subvarieties of the Poisson Lie group.  This is discussed with further detail in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 4]{Shapiro}.  In particular, one can compare the Poisson Lie group with the Zastava space for the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Recall that  moduli spaces of (non-periodic) monopoles on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be modelled by spaces of framed maps from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the flag variety <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G/B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, sending <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>[B]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (this is Jarvis&#39;s description of monopoles via scattering data <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Jarvis}).  The space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Map}_{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, G/B)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of monopoles of degree <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> (where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a positive coroot, identified as a class in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mr</span> H_<span class="pl-c1">2</span>(G/B;<span class="pl-c1">\ZZ</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) admits a compactification known as <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Zastava space}.  Concretely, this is a stratified algebraic variety, with stratification given by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1351" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1351"></td>
