        <td id="LC1351" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>Z_{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}(G) = <span class="pl-c1">\coprod</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span> <span class="pl-c1">\preceq</span> <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>} <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Map}_{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^1, G/B) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> <span class="pl-c1">\sym</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1352" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1352"></td>
        <td id="LC1352" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the factor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sym</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}(<span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> represents the space of coloured divisors <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{z_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D} <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i} = <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span> - <span class="pl-c1">\beta</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Zastava spaces were introduced by Bezrukavnikov and Finkelberg in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{BezrukavnikovFinkelbergI}, see also <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{BravermanICM}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1353" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1353"></td>
        <td id="LC1353" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1354" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1354"></td>
        <td id="LC1354" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Using a birational map to this Zastava space, GKLO showed that the union of symplectic leaves corresponding to representations of a given type (meaning a given sum <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sum</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) is equivalent to the union of the classical leaves of that given type.  It is, therefore, reasonable to conjecture that the decompositions of these two varieties into their individual symplectic leaves (i.e. into decompositions of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sum</span> <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> labelled by points in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) should coincide.  We should note that this doesn&#39;t seem to follow directly from the GKLO calculations.  They analyzed the symplectic leaves corresponding to the classical limits of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules via a rational map, denoted by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e_i(z) = b_i(z)/a_i(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, defined on an open set of this symplectic leaf.  This rational map is, by construction, not sensitive to the positions of the singularities, only of the total type of a representation.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1355" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1355"></td>
        <td id="LC1355" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1356" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1356"></td>
        <td id="LC1356" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Nevertheless, the symplectic leaves obtained as classical limits of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-modules <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>M_{D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{are} symplectic subvarieties of the Poisson Lie group sweeping out the union of symplectic leaves of a given type.  In particular every symplectic leaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> quantizes to some module within the GKLO classification, as claimed.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1357" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1357"></td>
        <td id="LC1357" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1358" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1358"></td>
        <td id="LC1358" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{example}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1359" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1359"></td>
        <td id="LC1359" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">One example is given by the case where the only pole lies at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">0</span> <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> <span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, so the map to the Poisson Lie group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> factors through the polynomial group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[z^{-1}]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  This example is included in the work of Kamnitzer, Webster, Weekes and Yacobi <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KWWY}.  They calculate the quantization of slices in the thick affine Grassmannian <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G(<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>(t^{-1})<span class="pl-cce">\!</span>)/G[t]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The thick affine Grassmannian has an open cell isomorphic to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  For each dominant coweight <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> there is a slice defining a symplectic leaf in this open cell: it&#39;s exactly the leaf corresponding to multiplicative Higgs fields with a single pole at 0 with degree <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Kamnitzer et al quantize this slice (in particular; they also quantize slices through to the other cells in the thick affine Grassmannian) to a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-module of GKLO type. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1360" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1360"></td>
        <td id="LC1360" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{example}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1361" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1361"></td>
        <td id="LC1361" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1362" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1362"></td>
        <td id="LC1362" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1363" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1363"></td>
        <td id="LC1363" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This result should be compared to the conjecture made in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Chapter 8.1]{NekrasovPestun}.  The Poisson Lie group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> receives a Poisson map from the full moduli space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{fr,sing}}(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of multiplicative Higgs bundles with arbitrary singularities.  Upon deformation quantization therefore, the quantized algebra of functions on this moduli space is closely related to the Yangian.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1364" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1364"></td>
        <td id="LC1364" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1365" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1365"></td>
        <td id="LC1365" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1366" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1366"></td>
        <td id="LC1366" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}[<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Opers and Quantization]</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1367" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1367"></td>
        <td id="LC1367" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Finally, let us refer back to Remark <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{q_opers_remark} and discuss the brane of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-opers, and the associated structures that should arise after quantization.  Recall that the multiplicative Hitchin system has a natural section defined by post-composition with the Steinberg section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G/G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The moduli space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-opers is the subspace of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\qconn</span>_G(C,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defined to be the multiplicative Hitchin section after rotating to the point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the twistor sphere of complex structures.  A difference version of the moduli space of opers was studied in the work of Mukhin and Varchenko <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{MukhinVarchenko}; it would be valuable to compare this definition, directly in the language of difference operators, with our approach to opers via the multiplicative Hitchin section, paralleling the work of Beilinson and Drinfeld in the additive case <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Section 3.1]{BDHitchin}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1368" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1368"></td>
        <td id="LC1368" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1369" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1369"></td>
        <td id="LC1369" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, we expect that the space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-opers will, in the rational case, be Lagrangian, and therefore will admit a canonical <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> P_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-structure -- a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>-<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-shifted Poisson structure -- on its derived algebra of functions.  It would be interesting to study the quantization of this <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span> P_<span class="pl-c1">0</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-algebra, and to investigate its relationship with the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-W algebras of Sevostyanov <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Knight,STSSevostyanov, Sevostyanov}, of Aganagic-Frenkel-Okounkov <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{AFO}, and of Avan-Frappat-Ragoucy <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{AvanFrappatRagoucy}.  We&#39;ll now proceed to discuss some first steps in this direction.  Preliminary results were announced by the second author at String-Math 2017 <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{PestunStringMath}.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1370" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1370"></td>
        <td id="LC1370" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1371" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1371"></td>
        <td id="LC1371" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1372" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1372"></td>
        <td id="LC1372" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\section</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Opers and <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Characters} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{qchar_section}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1373" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1373"></td>
        <td id="LC1373" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1374" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1374"></td>
        <td id="LC1374" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this final section we will discuss the space of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Opers in more depth.  In particular we will connect the geometric setup described in this paper, in terms of multiplicative Higgs bundles, to the gauge theoretic story studied by the second author and collaborators <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestunShatashvili,Kimura:2015rgi,Nekrasov:2015wsu}.  The main goal of this subsection will be to describe and motivate a connection between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-Opers and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-character maps from the theory of quantum groups <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FrenkelReshetikhinSTS,FrenkelReshetikhin2,FrenkelReshetikhin1,Sevostyanov,STSSevostyanov,Sevostyanov1}.  In order to make our statements as concrete as possible it will be useful to first describe the Steinberg section <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Steinberg} of a semisimple group explicitly.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1375" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1375"></td>
        <td id="LC1375" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1376" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1376"></td>
        <td id="LC1376" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Throughout this section, assume that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is a simple, simply-laced and simply-connected Lie group with Lie algebra <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\Delta</span> = <span class="pl-cce">\{</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_r<span class="pl-cce">\}</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be the set of simple roots of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In order to define the Steinberg section uniquely we&#39;ll fix a <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{pinning} on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  That is, choose a Borel subgroup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with maximal torus <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> and unipotent radical <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and choose a generator <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>e_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> for each simple root space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>_{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1377" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1377"></td>
        <td id="LC1377" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1378" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1378"></td>
        <td id="LC1378" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We&#39;ll also choose an element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>_i <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> N(T)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the normalizer of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> representing each element of the Weyl group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W = N(T)/T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The Steinberg section will be independent of this choice up to conjugation by a unique element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and independent of the ordering on the set of simple roots.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1379" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1379"></td>
        <td id="LC1379" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1380" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1380"></td>
        <td id="LC1380" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{Steinberg_section_def}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1381" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1381"></td>
        <td id="LC1381" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Steinberg section} of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> associated to a choice of pinning is the image of the injective map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> T/W <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defined by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1382" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1382"></td>
        <td id="LC1382" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>(t_1, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, t_r) = <span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{i=1}^r <span class="pl-c1">\exp</span>(t_i e_i) <span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>_i.<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1383" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1383"></td>
        <td id="LC1383" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Steinberg proved <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>[Theorem 1.4]{Steinberg} that, after restriction to the regular locus in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defines a section of the Chevalley map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> G <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1384" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1384"></td>
        <td id="LC1384" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1385" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1385"></td>
        <td id="LC1385" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1386" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1386"></td>
        <td id="LC1386" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{mhitch_section_def}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1387" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1387"></td>
        <td id="LC1387" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Fix a coloured divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{multiplicative Hitchin section} of the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the image <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhitch</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the map defined by post-composing a meromorphic <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued function on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with the Steinberg map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1388" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1388"></td>
        <td id="LC1388" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1389" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1389"></td>
        <td id="LC1389" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1390" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1390"></td>
        <td id="LC1390" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1391" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1391"></td>
        <td id="LC1391" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The multiplicative Hitchin section is indeed a section of the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\pi</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> after restricting to the connected component in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> corresponding to the trivial bundle, provided one chooses a value for the framing within the Steinberg section.  For example, if we choose the identity framing on the multiplicative Hitchin basis then the multiplicative Hitchin section lands in multiplicative Higgs bundles with framing <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>c = <span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>(<span class="pl-c1">1</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> at infinity, i.e. framing given by a Coxeter element.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1392" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1392"></td>
        <td id="LC1392" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1393" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1393"></td>
        <td id="LC1393" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1394" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1394"></td>
        <td id="LC1394" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, let&#39;s introduce the key idea in this section: the notion of <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{triangularization} for the multiplicative Hitchin section.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1395" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1395"></td>
        <td id="LC1395" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{gen_evals_def}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1396" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1396"></td>
        <td id="LC1396" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> be an element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhitch</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  We&#39;ll abusively identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with its image under the restriction map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>r_<span class="pl-c1">\infty</span> <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>,D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G_c[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to a formal neighbourhood of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  Say that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{generalized eigenvalues} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> T[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if there exists an element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> such that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u(z)g(z)u(z)^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_-[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_-<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the opposite Borel subgroup to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, which maps to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the canonical projection.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1397" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1397"></td>
        <td id="LC1397" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1398" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1398"></td>
        <td id="LC1398" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We say that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-generalized eigenvalues} <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> T[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> if there exists an element <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>U[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> such that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u(q^{-1}z)g(z)u(z)^{-1}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B_-[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> that maps to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the canonical projection. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1399" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1399"></td>
        <td id="LC1399" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1400" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1400"></td>
        <td id="LC1400" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1401" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1401"></td>
        <td id="LC1401" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1402" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1402"></td>
        <td id="LC1402" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In this setup <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the automorphism of the formal disk obtained by restricting an automorphism of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> or <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\CC</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\times</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to its formal punctured neighbourhood.  In particular we&#39;ll use this notation for the additive deformation we denoted by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\eps</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in previous sections, even though we&#39;ll use the multiplicative notation.  We make this notational choice in order to allow more direct comparison with the previous gauge theory literature.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1403" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1403"></td>
        <td id="LC1403" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1404" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1404"></td>
        <td id="LC1404" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1405" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1405"></td>
        <td id="LC1405" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It&#39;s sometimes useful to use a slightly different representation of the multiplicative Hitchin section, packaging the singularity datum in a more uniform way. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1406" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1406"></td>
        <td id="LC1406" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1407" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1407"></td>
        <td id="LC1407" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Choose a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the multiplicative Hitchin base <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. By clearing denominators, we can identify <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with a canonical polynomial <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t&#39;(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T[z]/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of fixed degree <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, with fixed top degree term.  Specifically, one finds</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1408" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1408"></td>
        <td id="LC1408" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>d_i = <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{z_j <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D} <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_j}(<span class="pl-c1">\lambda</span>_i)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1409" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1409"></td>
        <td id="LC1409" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\lambda</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i^<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{th}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fundamental weight.  We&#39;ll denote the locus of polynomials of this form by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T[z]_d<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1410" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1410"></td>
        <td id="LC1410" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1411" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1411"></td>
        <td id="LC1411" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We define an embedding from <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T[z]_d/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> into <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> as follows.  First, we encode the data of the coloured divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in terms of a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued polynomial.  That is, we set </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1412" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1412"></td>
        <td id="LC1412" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>p_i(z) = <span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{z_j <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> D} (z-z_j)^{<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_{z_j}(<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_i)}<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1413" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1413"></td>
        <td id="LC1413" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_j<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>j^{<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{th}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fundamental weight.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1414" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1414"></td>
        <td id="LC1414" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1415" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1415"></td>
        <td id="LC1415" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1416" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1416"></td>
        <td id="LC1416" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted multiplicative Hitchin section} is the image of the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>&#39; <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> T[z]_d/W <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> G(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> defined by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1417" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1417"></td>
        <td id="LC1417" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{equation}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1418" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1418"></td>
        <td id="LC1418" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{eq:steinberg}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1419" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1419"></td>
        <td id="LC1419" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>&#39;(t(z)) = <span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{i=1}^r <span class="pl-c1">\exp\left</span>(t&#39;_{i}(z) e_i<span class="pl-c1">\right</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>_i p_i(z)^{-<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_i}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1420" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1420"></td>
        <td id="LC1420" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{equation}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1421" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1421"></td>
        <td id="LC1421" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i^<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{th}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fundamental coweight.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1422" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1422"></td>
        <td id="LC1422" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1423" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1423"></td>
        <td id="LC1423" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1424" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1424"></td>
        <td id="LC1424" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">This <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted section is obtained from the ordinary multiplicative Hitchin section after conjugation by an element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G[z]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  The result is no longer directly related to the multiplicative Hitchin moduli space because this conjugation breaks the framing at <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\infty</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  It is, however, sometimes useful for computation. One can define the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-triangularization of a point in this <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted section exactly as in the ordinary case.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1425" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1425"></td>
        <td id="LC1425" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1426" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1426"></td>
        <td id="LC1426" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Now, let&#39;s introduce the other main object we&#39;ll be discussing in this section.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1427" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1427"></td>
        <td id="LC1427" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1428" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1428"></td>
        <td id="LC1428" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{definition}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1429" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1429"></td>
        <td id="LC1429" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-character} is an algebra homomorphism </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1430" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1430"></td>
        <td id="LC1430" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>_q <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Rep}(Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>)) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(T_1[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1431" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1431"></td>
        <td id="LC1431" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">from the ring of finite-dimensional representations of the Yangian to the ring of functions on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, first defined by Knight <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Knight}.  Given a choice of singularity datum <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> one can define a linear map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)^* <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mr</span>{Rep}(Y(<span class="pl-c1">\gg</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> generated by the map identifying a coordinate functional on the multiplicative Hitchin base space with the irreducible representation with the given highest weight.  We&#39;ll abusively also denote the composite map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)^* <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(T_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>[[z^{-1}]])<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>_q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1432" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1432"></td>
        <td id="LC1432" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{definition}</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1434" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1434"></td>
        <td id="LC1434" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-twisted fundamental <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-characters <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t&#39;_i(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are obtained by recursive Weyl reflections of the form <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun,NekrasovPestunShatashvili,Nekrasov:2015wsu} (following the conventions from <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Kimura:2015rgi} for shifts)</td>

        <td id="LC1436" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">  w <span class="pl-c1">\cdot</span>_q y_i(z)) = y_{i}(z q^{-1})^{-1} <span class="pl-c1">\Bigg</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{e: i <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> j} y_j(z) <span class="pl-c1">\Bigg</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\Bigg</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{e: j<span class="pl-c1">\to</span> i} y_j(q^{-1} z)<span class="pl-c1">\Bigg</span>)  p_{i}( q^{-1} z).</td>

        <td id="L1441" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1441"></td>
        <td id="LC1441" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">These formulae appeared previously in <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestun, NekrasovPestunShatashvili} and</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1444" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1444"></td>
        <td id="LC1444" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the undeformed case, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-functions have a very geometric meaning: they are equivalent to a sequence of algebraic functions defining the cameral cover at a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the Hitchin base.  The cameral cover associated to a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the multiplicative Hitchin base is, to put it briefly, obtained away from the singular locus as the fiber product <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> C_b^<span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> = (<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_z <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span>_{T/W} T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, where the map <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_z <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the meromorphic map corresponding to <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  In other words, the closed points of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> C^<span class="pl-c1">\circ</span>_b<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are simply pairs <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(z, y) <span class="pl-c1">\in</span> (<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D) <span class="pl-c1">\times</span> T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> such that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z) = [y]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  One can obtain the cameral curve as the graph of a <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>|W|<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1445" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1445"></td>
        <td id="LC1445" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">meromorphic function <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span> <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1446" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1446"></td>
        <td id="LC1446" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">taking all images <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> under the projection <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y <span class="pl-c1">\mapsto</span> [y]<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where elements of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1447" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1447"></td>
        <td id="LC1447" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">coordinatized as  <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\prod</span>_{i = 1}^{r} y_i^{<span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i^{<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\alpha</span>_i^{<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are simple coroots.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1448" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1448"></td>
        <td id="LC1448" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Then, on a contractible local patch in the complement of the ramification locus define <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t_i(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to be the sum </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1449" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1449"></td>
        <td id="LC1449" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>t_i(z) = <span class="pl-c1">\sum</span>_{y <span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{ over } b} <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_i(y(z)),<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1450" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1450"></td>
        <td id="LC1450" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">where the sum is over all local lifts <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>T/W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued function <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>b(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and where <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_i <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> T <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{C}^{<span class="pl-c1">\times</span>}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>u^<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{th}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fundamental weight. Because of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>W<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-invariance, for each <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> these local descriptions glue together to define a global <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mathbb</span>{C}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-valued function on the curve <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>_z <span class="pl-c1">\bs</span> D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1451" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1451"></td>
        <td id="LC1451" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1452" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1452"></td>
        <td id="LC1452" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">In the classical limit <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q=<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> the procedure of taking generalized eigenvalues and the character map are closely related, simply because the multiplicative Hitchin section is a section of the Hitchin fibration.  The character map, evaluated in the fundamental representations associated to the fundamental weights <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\ldots</span>, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_r<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, is essentially the Chevalley map sending a matrix to its characteristic polynomial.  In other words it is essentially the multiplicative Hitchin fibration itself.  Therefore, we find that </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1453" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1453"></td>
        <td id="LC1453" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>(t_i)(<span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>(b(z))) = t_i(z)<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1454" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1454"></td>
        <td id="LC1454" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">up to an affine isomorphism.  The same holds when we replace <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\sigma</span>(b(z))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> by <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, its triangularization, because the maps <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>(t_i)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are adjoint-invariant.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1455" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1455"></td>
        <td id="LC1455" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1456" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1456"></td>
        <td id="LC1456" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">We conjecture that this relationship survives after <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-deformation, yielding the following relationship between <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-opers and the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-character.  This expectation is motivated in part by the multiplicative geometric Langlands Conjecture <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{multLanglands} applied to the canonical coisotropic A-brane -- quantizing the ring of Poisson commuting functions on the multiplicative Hitchin system -- whose Langlands dual is expected to be precisely the brane of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-opers.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1457" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1457"></td>
        <td id="LC1457" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>

        <td id="LC1458" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{conjecture} <span class="pl-c1">\label</span>{qchar_conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1459" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1459"></td>
        <td id="LC1459" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1460" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1460"></td>
        <td id="LC1460" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> For any <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, every element of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> of <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhitch</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\fr</span>_G(<span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span>, D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> has a unique <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> generalized eigenvalue, and therefore there is a well-defined map</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1461" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1461"></td>
        <td id="LC1461" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-cce">\[</span>E_q <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>) <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> T[[z^{-1}]] <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> G[[z^{-1}]]<span class="pl-cce">\]</span></td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1462" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1462"></td>
        <td id="LC1462" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">given by applying the multiplicative Hitchin section then computing its <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-generalized eigenvalues.  </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1463" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1463"></td>
        <td id="LC1463" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1464" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1464"></td>
        <td id="LC1464" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\item</span> The composite <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>E_q^* <span class="pl-c1">\circ</span> <span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>_q <span class="pl-c1">\colon</span> <span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)^* <span class="pl-c1">\to</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is an affine isomorphism onto the space of linear functionals <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)^* <span class="pl-c1">\sub</span> <span class="pl-c1">\OO</span>(<span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1465" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1465"></td>

      <tr>
        <td id="L1466" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1466"></td>
        <td id="LC1466" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{conjecture}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1467" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1467"></td>
        <td id="LC1467" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1468" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1468"></td>
        <td id="LC1468" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">Let&#39;s demonstrate this conjecture in a few examples.  In each case we&#39;ll describe the multiplicative Hitchin section, and then calculate an inverse to the map sending a point <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the base space <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mc</span> B(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> to the corresponding generalized eigenvalue map for the Hitchin section <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>.  If <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y_i(t(z))<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> is the composite of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-generalized eigenvalue map with the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i^<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{th}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> fundamental weight <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, we must verify that <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\chi</span>_q(y_i(t)) = t_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>i^<span class="pl-c1">\text</span>{th}<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> coordinate map (up to an affine isomorphism).</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

        <td id="LC1488" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">It&#39;s easy to solve the equation <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>g^t = u(q^{-1}z)g^y(z) u^{-1}(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> explicitly.         <td id="L1517" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1517"></td>
        <td id="LC1517" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">and that indeed coincides with the expression for the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-characters for the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>A_<span class="pl-c1">2</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> quiver appearing in</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1518" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1518"></td>
        <td id="LC1518" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{Nekrasov:2015wsu,NekrasovPestunShatashvili,NekrasovPestun,Kimura:2015rgi}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1519" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1519"></td>
        <td id="LC1519" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1520" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1520"></td>
        <td id="LC1520" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">\item The first example for which the condition that the composite map in Conjecture \ref{qchar_conjecture} is a non-trivial affine isomorphism occurs for the $D_4$ Dynkin diagram, for instance for the group $G = \SO(8)$.  In that case, even for $q=1$ we find the composite $E^* \circ \chi$, i.e. the result of applying the character map in the fundamental representations given by fundamental weights $(\omega_1, \omega_2,\omega_2,\omega_4)$ to the Steinberg section, is not quite the identity, but rather than map sending $(t_1,t_2,t_3,t_4)$ to $(t_1,t_2+1,t_3,t_4)$.  One sees this by considering the $G$-modules associated to irreducible finite-dimensional highest weight modules of the Yangian $Y(\gg)$ in the limit $q \to 1$: the 29-dimensional module induced in this way from the fundamental weight $\omega_2$ splits as the sum of the 28 dimensional adjoint representation associated to the fundamental weight $\omega_2$ and the trivial representation.  We include some calculations verifying the conjecture for $G=\SO(8)$ in Appendix \ref{D4_appendix}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1521" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1521"></td>
        <td id="LC1521" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{enumerate}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1522" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1522"></td>
        <td id="LC1522" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{examples}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1523" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1523"></td>
        <td id="LC1523" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">
</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1524" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1524"></td>
        <td id="LC1524" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1525" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1525"></td>
        <td id="LC1525" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">After triangularizing, an element of the multiplicative Hitchin section transforms into a function on <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\bb</span>{CP}^<span class="pl-c1">1</span><span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> with apparent singularities (even away from the divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>D<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>) where the functions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y_{i}(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> have zeroes and poles.  However, when we apply the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-character map these singularities are cancelled in pairs between the monomial summands of Equation <span class="pl-c1">\ref</span>{iWeyl_action}, as we sum over the transformation by each element of the Weyl group.  This cancellation property has been called ``regularity of the <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>q<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>-character&#39;&#39; in the quantum group representation theory literature <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{FrenkelReshetikhin1,FrenkelReshetikhin2} as well as in the gauge theoretic construction of <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestunShatashvili,Nekrasov:2015wsu,NekrasovPestun,Kimura:2015rgi}.</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1526" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1526"></td>
        <td id="LC1526" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1527" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1527"></td>
        <td id="LC1527" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">The meromorphic functions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y_{i}(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be expressed as ratios of the form <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>y_{i}(z) = Q_{i}(z)/Q_i(q^{-1}z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, and the zeroes of the functions denoted <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>Q_i<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are known as <span class="pl-c1">\emph</span>{Bethe roots} in the context of the Bethe ansatz equations.  In this language, the Bethe ansatz equations are precisely the equations which ensures that poles in <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>t_{i}(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> are cancelled. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1528" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1528"></td>
        <td id="LC1528" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"><span class="pl-c1">\end</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

</td>

        <td id="L1530" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1530"></td>
        <td id="LC1530" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> <span class="pl-c1">\begin</span>{remark}</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1531" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1531"></td>
        <td id="LC1531" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   Some of the results in a recent paper by Koroteev, Sage and Zeitlin <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{KoroteevSageZeitlin} seem to overlap</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1532" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1532"></td>
        <td id="LC1532" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   with the specialization of the main conjecture of this section to the group <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>G  = <span class="pl-c1">\SL</span>(N)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>, in the case where the the</td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1533" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1533"></td>
        <td id="LC1533" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   coweight coloured divisor <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> takes a particular form: where the functions <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>p_i(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> encoding <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span>(D,<span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> can be related to the ratio of Drinfeld polynomials <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_i(z)/<span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_i(q^{-1} z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> in the Bethe ansatz equations. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
        <td id="L1534" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1534"></td>
        <td id="LC1534" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   This special form for the singularity datum means that the Yangian module obtained by quantization of the symplectic leaf <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\mhiggs</span>_G(C,D, <span class="pl-c1">\omega</span>^<span class="pl-c1">\vee</span>)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span> contains (as a quotient) the finite-dimensional Drinfeld module specified by the Drinfeld polynomials <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">$</span><span class="pl-c1">\rho</span>_{i}(z)<span class="pl-pds">$</span></span>. In the relation to the occurence of the Bethe ansatz equations in quiver gauge theory <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{NekrasovPestunShatashvili}, this specialization is known as 4d to 2d specialization, and was first studied by Chen, Dorey, Hollowood and Lee <span class="pl-c1">\cite</span>{ChenDoreyHollowoodLee, DoreyHollowoodLee}. </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>

        <td id="L1573" class="blob-num js-line-number" data-line-number="1573"></td>
        <td id="LC1573" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line">   <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>

        <td id="LC1574" class="blob-code blob-code-inner js-file-line"> u_{6}= &amp;-<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{p_{2} p_{3} p_{4,-1}}{y_{4,-1}}-<span class="pl-c1">\frac</span>{p_{2} p_{3} y_{4}}{y_{2}} <span class="pl-c1">\\</span></td>
